  "content": "<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang=\"en\">\n<head>\n  <meta charset=\"UTF-8\">\n  <meta name=\"viewport\" content=\"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0\">\n  <title>Lesson 3 — Computing Edit Distance: The DP Table</title>\n  <link rel=\"stylesheet\" href=\"../assets/style.css\">\n  <style>\n    /* ── Stepper-specific styles ── */\n    #stepper-table td {\n      width: 2.6rem; height: 2.6rem;\n      font-size: 0.95rem; font-weight: 600;\n      transition: background 0.2s;\n      cursor: default;\n    }\n    #stepper-table td.empty { color: var(--rule); }\n    #stepper-table td.current { background: #bfdbfe; outline: 2px solid var(--accent); outline-offset: -2px; }\n    #stepper-table td.used-diag { background: #fef9c3; }\n    #stepper-table td.used-top  { background: #dcfce7; }\n    #stepper-table td.used-left { background: #fce7f3; }\n    #stepper-table td.settled   { background: var(--code-bg); }\n    #stepper-table td.path      { background: var(--success-bg); font-weight: 900; }\n    #stepper-table th { background: var(--code-bg); font-weight: 700; font-size: 0.88rem; }\n    .legend { display:flex; gap:1rem; flex-wrap:wrap; font-family:var(--sans); font-size:0.8rem; margin:0.6rem 0 1rem; }\n    .legend span { display:flex; align-items:center; gap:0.35rem; }\n    .legend .swatch { width:1rem; height:1rem; border-radius:2px; border:1px solid var(--rule); flex-shrink:0; }\n    #step-explanation {\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.9rem;\n      background: var(--accent-bg); border-radius: 6px;\n      padding: 0.8rem 1rem; margin: 0.75rem 0; min-height: 3.5rem;\n      line-height: 1.5;\n    }\n    #step-explanation code { font-size: 0.85em; }\n    .op-row { display:flex; gap:0.5rem; flex-wrap:wrap; margin-top:0.5rem; }\n    .op-badge {\n      font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 0.78rem; padding: 0.2rem 0.6rem;\n      border-radius: 4px; border: 1px solid var(--rule); background: #fff;\n    }\n    .op-badge.diag  { background:#fef9c3; border-color:#ca8a04; }\n    .op-badge.top   { background:#dcfce7; border-color:#16a34a; }\n    .op-badge.left  { background:#fce7f3; border-color:#db2777; }\n    .op-badge.chosen{ font-weight:700; outline:2px solid var(--ink); outline-offset:1px; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 3 of 6</div>\n  <h1>Computing Edit Distance: The DP Table</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: use dynamic programming to find the minimum in polynomial time</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  We know edit distance is the right metric. But how do you\n  <em>compute</em> it? The naïve approach — try every possible sequence of\n  edits and keep the shortest — has exponential time complexity.\n  For a 10-character query against a 50-character filename, that's\n  trillions of paths to evaluate.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  Observe that the problem has <strong>overlapping subproblems</strong>:\n  the edit distance between the first 4 characters of A and the first 3\n  characters of B is a subproblem of the full computation — and it\n  gets used many times. Store those subproblem answers in a table and\n  look them up instead of recomputing them. This is <strong>dynamic programming</strong>.\n  Time complexity drops from exponential to O(m × n).\n</div>\n\n<h2>The recurrence relation</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Define <code>dp[i][j]</code> as the edit distance between the first\n  <code>i</code> characters of string A and the first <code>j</code>\n  characters of string B.\n</p>\n\n<p>There are only ever three cases when filling a cell:</p>\n\n<pre>If A[i] == B[j]:          dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j-1]          // no edit needed\n\nIf A[i] != B[j]:          dp[i][j] = 1 + min(\n                              dp[i-1][j-1],  // substitute\n                              dp[i-1][j],    // delete from A\n                              dp[i][j-1]     // insert into A\n                           )</pre>\n\n<p>\n  The base cases initialise the first row and column: converting an\n  empty string to a k-character string costs exactly k operations.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why three predecessors?</span>\n  Each cell in the table represents a prefix-pair. To get here, either:\n  <ul style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;\">\n    <li>The last characters matched (come from the diagonal — free move)</li>\n    <li>We deleted a character from A (come from above — cost 1)</li>\n    <li>We inserted a character into A (come from the left — cost 1)</li>\n  </ul>\n  The substitute case is the diagonal with a cost of 1 when characters differ.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Step through the table</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to fill the table one cell at a time.\n  Each step shows you which three predecessor cells were consulted and\n  which operation was chosen. When the table is complete, the\n  <strong>optimal path</strong> is traced back in green.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\" style=\"padding:1.1rem 1.2rem;\">\n  <h3>DP Table Stepper</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:120px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">String A (rows)</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"str-a\" value=\"comit\" maxlength=\"9\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:120px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">String B (columns)</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"str-b\" value=\"commit\" maxlength=\"9\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"display:flex;align-items:flex-end;\">\n      <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" id=\"reset-btn\" onclick=\"resetStepper()\">Reset</button>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div class=\"dp-table-wrapper\">\n    <table id=\"stepper-table\" class=\"dp-table\"></table>\n  </div>\n\n  <div class=\"legend\">\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#bfdbfe;border-color:#3b82f6;\"></span> Current cell</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#fef9c3;border-color:#ca8a04;\"></span> Diagonal (sub / match)</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#dcfce7;border-color:#16a34a;\"></span> Above (delete)</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#fce7f3;border-color:#db2777;\"></span> Left (insert)</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:var(--success-bg);border-color:var(--success);\"></span> Optimal path</span>\n  </div>\n\n  <div id=\"step-explanation\">Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.</div>\n\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.6rem;margin-top:0.5rem;flex-wrap:wrap;\">\n    <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" id=\"next-btn\" onclick=\"nextStep()\">Next Step</button>\n    <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"runToEnd()\">Run to end</button>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Reading the finished table</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The answer is always in the <strong>bottom-right cell</strong>:\n  <code>dp[m][n]</code>, where m and n are the lengths of the two strings.\n  The path from bottom-right back to top-left (tracing the minimum choices)\n  tells you exactly which edits were made — a full alignment of the strings.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  For fuzzy search, we only need the number in that final cell. Computing the\n  full path (the <em>alignment</em>) is an optional extra step used when you\n  want to highlight which characters matched.\n</p>\n\n<h2>Complexity</h2>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"margin:1rem 0;\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr><th>Approach</th><th>Time</th><th>Space</th></tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td>Naïve recursion (no memoisation)</td><td>O(3<sup>m</sup>)</td><td>O(m)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>DP table (Wagner–Fischer)</td><td>O(m × n)</td><td>O(m × n)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>DP table, two-row optimised</td><td>O(m × n)</td><td>O(n)</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Space optimisation</span>\n  Each row only needs the previous row's values, so you can discard all but\n  the last two rows. This reduces space from O(m × n) to O(n) — important\n  when scanning many candidates.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. In the DP table, what does <code>dp[0][j]</code> (the entire first row) always equal, and why?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> Always 0 — no edits are needed for empty strings</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Always j — inserting j characters to build B from an empty A</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Always 1 — only one edit is ever needed per row</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> Always the length of B — matching the full string is the base case</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. dp[0][j] = j because converting an empty string to the first j characters of B requires exactly j insertions.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. When filling cell <code>dp[i][j]</code> and A[i] ≠ B[j], the formula is <code>1 + min(dp[i-1][j-1], dp[i-1][j], dp[i][j-1])</code>. Which predecessor corresponds to <em>inserting</em> a character into A?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> dp[i-1][j-1] — the diagonal cell</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> dp[i-1][j]   — the cell directly above</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> dp[i][j-1]   — the cell directly to the left</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> dp[i+1][j+1] — the cell diagonally below-right</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','c','Correct. Moving left means B is one character shorter — equivalent to inserting a character into A to account for that extra character in B.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. Why does dynamic programming reduce the time complexity from exponential to O(m × n)?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> It uses bitwise operations to compare characters faster</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> It avoids recomputing the same subproblem answers by storing them in a table</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> It only computes cells on the diagonal of the table</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> It prunes paths that exceed the threshold before completing them</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. Naïve recursion recomputes the same prefix-pair subproblems exponentially many times. DP stores each answer once and looks it up in O(1), so each of the m×n cells is filled exactly once.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. Where in the completed DP table do you read off the final edit distance?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> The top-left cell dp[0][0]</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> The cell with the smallest value in the table</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> The bottom-right cell dp[m][n]</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> The sum of all values along the main diagonal</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','c','Correct. dp[m][n] holds the edit distance between the full string A (length m) and the full string B (length n).')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://www.baeldung.com/cs/levenshtein-distance-computation\" target=\"_blank\">\n    Levenshtein Distance Computation — Baeldung on Computer Science\n  </a>\n  — Works through the DP table step-by-step with diagrams. Reading this\n  alongside the stepper above will solidify the recurrence relation.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat and I'll explain, rephrase, or go deeper on any cell, step, or formula from this lesson.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0002-edit-distance.html\">← Lesson 2: Edit Distance</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 3 of 6</span>\n  <a href=\"0004-threshold-search.html\">Next: From Distance to Search →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── DP Stepper ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nlet A, B, dp, steps, stepIdx, done;\n\nfunction buildSteps(a, b) {\n  const m = a.length, n = b.length;\n  const table = Array.from({length: m+1}, (_, i) =>\n    Array.from({length: n+1}, (_, j) => i===0 ? j : j===0 ? i : null)\n  );\n  const seq = [];\n  // Emit base-case cells as pre-settled (no explanation needed)\n  for (let i = 1; i <= m; i++)\n    for (let j = 1; j <= n; j++) {\n      const diag = table[i-1][j-1];\n      const top  = table[i-1][j];\n      const left = table[i][j-1];\n      const match = a[i-1] === b[j-1];\n      let val, op;\n      if (match) {\n        val = diag; op = 'match';\n      } else {\n        const best = Math.min(diag, top, left);\n        val = 1 + best;\n        op = best === diag ? 'sub' : best === top ? 'del' : 'ins';\n      }\n      table[i][j] = val;\n      seq.push({i, j, val, op, match, diag, top, left});\n    }\n  return {table, seq};\n}\n\nfunction resetStepper() {\n  A = document.getElementById('str-a').value || 'comit';\n  B = document.getElementById('str-b').value || 'commit';\n  const built = buildSteps(A, B);\n  dp = built.table; steps = built.seq; stepIdx = 0; done = false;\n  renderTable();\n  document.getElementById('step-explanation').innerHTML = 'Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.';\n  document.getElementById('next-btn').disabled = false;\n}\n\nfunction renderTable(highlightStep, showPath) {\n  const m = A.length, n = B.length;\n  const tbl = document.getElementById('stepper-table');\n  let html = '<thead><tr><th></th><th>ε</th>';\n  for (let j = 0; j < n; j++) html += `<th>${B[j]}</th>`;\n  html += '</tr></thead><tbody>';\n  for (let i = 0; i <= m; i++) {\n    html += '<tr>';\n    html += `<th>${i === 0 ? 'ε' : A[i-1]}</th>`;\n    for (let j = 0; j <= n; j++) {\n      const val = dp[i][j];\n      let cls = '';\n      if (showPath && showPath.some(p => p[0]===i && p[1]===j)) cls = 'path';\n      else if (highlightStep) {\n        const {i:ci, j:cj} = highlightStep;\n        if      (i===ci   && j===cj)   cls = 'current';\n        else if (i===ci-1 && j===cj-1) cls = 'used-diag';\n        else if (i===ci-1 && j===cj)   cls = 'used-top';\n        else if (i===ci   && j===cj-1) cls = 'used-left';\n        else if (val !== null && !(i===ci && j===cj)) cls = 'settled';\n      } else if (val !== null) cls = 'settled';\n      const display = val === null ? '·' : val;\n      html += `<td class=\"${cls}\">${display}</td>`;\n    }\n    html += '</tr>';\n  }\n  html += '</tbody>';\n  tbl.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nfunction nextStep() {\n  if (done) return;\n  if (stepIdx >= steps.length) { finishStepper(); return; }\n  const s = steps[stepIdx];\n  // Temporarily null out cells not yet processed\n  for (let k = stepIdx; k < steps.length; k++) {\n    dp[steps[k].i][steps[k].j] = null;\n  }\n  dp[s.i][s.j] = s.val;\n  renderTable(s);\n\n  const ai = A[s.i - 1], bj = B[s.j - 1];\n  let html = '';\n  if (s.match) {\n    html = `<strong>Cell [${s.i},${s.j}]</strong>: A[${s.i}]='<code>${ai}</code>' matches B[${s.j}]='<code>${bj}</code>' — no edit needed. ` +\n           `Carry diagonal: <code>dp[${s.i-1}][${s.j-1}] = ${s.diag}</code> → <strong>${s.val}</strong>`;\n  } else {\n    const ops = [\n      {label:'sub (diagonal)', val:s.diag, cls:'diag', chosen: s.op==='sub'},\n      {label:'del (above)',    val:s.top,  cls:'top',  chosen: s.op==='del'},\n      {label:'ins (left)',     val:s.left, cls:'left', chosen: s.op==='ins'},\n    ];\n    const chosen = ops.find(o => o.chosen);\n    html = `<strong>Cell [${s.i},${s.j}]</strong>: A[${s.i}]='<code>${ai}</code>' ≠ B[${s.j}]='<code>${bj}</code>' — pick cheapest operation + 1.`;\n    html += `<div class=\"op-row\">` + ops.map(o =>\n      `<span class=\"op-badge ${o.cls}${o.chosen ? ' chosen' : ''}\">${o.label}: ${o.val}</span>`\n    ).join('') + `</div>`;\n    html += `<span style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;display:block;\">Chose <strong>${chosen.label}</strong>: 1 + ${chosen.val} = <strong>${s.val}</strong></span>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('step-explanation').innerHTML = html;\n  stepIdx++;\n  if (stepIdx >= steps.length) {\n    document.getElementById('next-btn').textContent = 'Show Path';\n  }\n}\n\nfunction runToEnd() {\n  while (stepIdx < steps.length) {\n    const s = steps[stepIdx];\n    dp[s.i][s.j] = s.val;\n    stepIdx++;\n  }\n  finishStepper();\n}\n\nfunction finishStepper() {\n  done = true;\n  document.getElementById('next-btn').disabled = true;\n  document.getElementById('next-btn').textContent = 'Done';\n  const path = tracePath();\n  renderTable(null, path);\n  const dist = dp[A.length][B.length];\n  document.getElementById('step-explanation').innerHTML =\n    `<strong>Complete.</strong> Edit distance = <strong style=\"font-size:1.2rem;color:var(--success)\">${dist}</strong>. ` +\n    `The green path traces the optimal alignment from bottom-right back to top-left.`;\n}\n\nfunction tracePath() {\n  const path = [];\n  let i = A.length, j = B.length;\n  while (i > 0 || j > 0) {\n    path.push([i, j]);\n    if (i === 0) { j--; continue; }\n    if (j === 0) { i--; continue; }\n    const diag = dp[i-1][j-1], top = dp[i-1][j], left = dp[i][j-1];\n    if (A[i-1] === B[j-1] && dp[i][j] === diag) { i--; j--; }\n    else if (dp[i][j] === 1 + Math.min(diag, top, left)) {\n      const best = Math.min(diag, top, left);\n      if (best === diag) { i--; j--; }\n      else if (best === top) { i--; }\n      else { j--; }\n    }\n  }\n  path.push([0, 0]);\n  return path;\n}\n\n// Init\ndocument.getElementById('str-a').addEventListener('input', resetStepper);\ndocument.getElementById('str-b').addEventListener('input', resetStepper);\nresetStepper();\n\n// ── Quiz logic ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}

Opening in existing browser session.

Lesson 3 is open. This one is the most hands-on so far.

**The design decision it justifies**: naïve recursion tries every edit path — exponential. The DP table observes that sub-problems overlap (the distance between prefixes gets reused), so store each answer once and look it up. O(m×n) instead of O(3^m).

**The stepper** lets you walk through `comit` vs `commit` one cell at a time. Each step tells you:
- Which three predecessors were consulted (diagonal / above / left, colour-coded)
- Which character comparison happened
- Which operation was chosen and why
- The running value in the cell

Press **Run to end** to skip to the finished table, then the optimal alignment path highlights in green.

Try stepping through it manually a few times — change the strings to something shorter like `cat` vs `cart` if you want a smaller table to internalize first.

Come back when you're done and I'll open Lesson 4: turning a distance number into an actual search (threshold filtering and normalisation).

  "file_path": "/work/random/ai-teach-test/lessons/0003-dp-table.html",
  "content": "<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang=\"en\">\n<head>\n  <meta charset=\"UTF-8\">\n  <meta name=\"viewport\" content=\"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0\">\n  <title>Lesson 3 — Computing Edit Distance: The DP Table</title>\n  <link rel=\"stylesheet\" href=\"../assets/style.css\">\n  <style>\n    /* ── Stepper-specific styles ── */\n    #stepper-table td {\n      width: 2.6rem; height: 2.6rem;\n      font-size: 0.95rem; font-weight: 600;\n      transition: background 0.2s;\n      cursor: default;\n    }\n    #stepper-table td.empty { color: var(--rule); }\n    #stepper-table td.current { background: #bfdbfe; outline: 2px solid var(--accent); outline-offset: -2px; }\n    #stepper-table td.used-diag { background: #fef9c3; }\n    #stepper-table td.used-top  { background: #dcfce7; }\n    #stepper-table td.used-left { background: #fce7f3; }\n    #stepper-table td.settled   { background: var(--code-bg); }\n    #stepper-table td.path      { background: var(--success-bg); font-weight: 900; }\n    #stepper-table th { background: var(--code-bg); font-weight: 700; font-size: 0.88rem; }\n    .legend { display:flex; gap:1rem; flex-wrap:wrap; font-family:var(--sans); font-size:0.8rem; margin:0.6rem 0 1rem; }\n    .legend span { display:flex; align-items:center; gap:0.35rem; }\n    .legend .swatch { width:1rem; height:1rem; border-radius:2px; border:1px solid var(--rule); flex-shrink:0; }\n    #step-explanation {\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.9rem;\n      background: var(--accent-bg); border-radius: 6px;\n      padding: 0.8rem 1rem; margin: 0.75rem 0; min-height: 3.5rem;\n      line-height: 1.5;\n    }\n    #step-explanation code { font-size: 0.85em; }\n    .op-row { display:flex; gap:0.5rem; flex-wrap:wrap; margin-top:0.5rem; }\n    .op-badge {\n      font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 0.78rem; padding: 0.2rem 0.6rem;\n      border-radius: 4px; border: 1px solid var(--rule); background: #fff;\n    }\n    .op-badge.diag  { background:#fef9c3; border-color:#ca8a04; }\n    .op-badge.top   { background:#dcfce7; border-color:#16a34a; }\n    .op-badge.left  { background:#fce7f3; border-color:#db2777; }\n    .op-badge.chosen{ font-weight:700; outline:2px solid var(--ink); outline-offset:1px; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 3 of 6</div>\n  <h1>Computing Edit Distance: The DP Table</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: use dynamic programming to find the minimum in polynomial time</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  We know edit distance is the right metric. But how do you\n  <em>compute</em> it? The naïve approach — try every possible sequence of\n  edits and keep the shortest — has exponential time complexity.\n  For a 10-character query against a 50-character filename, that's\n  trillions of paths to evaluate.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  Observe that the problem has <strong>overlapping subproblems</strong>:\n  the edit distance between the first 4 characters of A and the first 3\n  characters of B is a subproblem of the full computation — and it\n  gets used many times. Store those subproblem answers in a table and\n  look them up instead of recomputing them. This is <strong>dynamic programming</strong>.\n  Time complexity drops from exponential to O(m × n).\n</div>\n\n<h2>The recurrence relation</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Define <code>dp[i][j]</code> as the edit distance between the first\n  <code>i</code> characters of string A and the first <code>j</code>\n  characters of string B.\n</p>\n\n<p>There are only ever three cases when filling a cell:</p>\n\n<pre>If A[i] == B[j]:          dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j-1]          // no edit needed\n\nIf A[i] != B[j]:          dp[i][j] = 1 + min(\n                              dp[i-1][j-1],  // substitute\n                              dp[i-1][j],    // delete from A\n                              dp[i][j-1]     // insert into A\n                           )</pre>\n\n<p>\n  The base cases initialise the first row and column: converting an\n  empty string to a k-character string costs exactly k operations.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why three predecessors?</span>\n  Each cell in the table represents a prefix-pair. To get here, either:\n  <ul style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;\">\n    <li>The last characters matched (come from the diagonal — free move)</li>\n    <li>We deleted a character from A (come from above — cost 1)</li>\n    <li>We inserted a character into A (come from the left — cost 1)</li>\n  </ul>\n  The substitute case is the diagonal with a cost of 1 when characters differ.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Step through the table</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to fill the table one cell at a time.\n  Each step shows you which three predecessor cells were consulted and\n  which operation was chosen. When the table is complete, the\n  <strong>optimal path</strong> is traced back in green.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\" style=\"padding:1.1rem 1.2rem;\">\n  <h3>DP Table Stepper</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:120px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">String A (rows)</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"str-a\" value=\"comit\" maxlength=\"9\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:120px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">String B (columns)</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"str-b\" value=\"commit\" maxlength=\"9\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"display:flex;align-items:flex-end;\">\n      <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" id=\"reset-btn\" onclick=\"resetStepper()\">Reset</button>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div class=\"dp-table-wrapper\">\n    <table id=\"stepper-table\" class=\"dp-table\"></table>\n  </div>\n\n  <div class=\"legend\">\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#bfdbfe;border-color:#3b82f6;\"></span> Current cell</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#fef9c3;border-color:#ca8a04;\"></span> Diagonal (sub / match)</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#dcfce7;border-color:#16a34a;\"></span> Above (delete)</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:#fce7f3;border-color:#db2777;\"></span> Left (insert)</span>\n    <span><span class=\"swatch\" style=\"background:var(--success-bg);border-color:var(--success);\"></span> Optimal path</span>\n  </div>\n\n  <div id=\"step-explanation\">Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.</div>\n\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.6rem;margin-top:0.5rem;flex-wrap:wrap;\">\n    <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" id=\"next-btn\" onclick=\"nextStep()\">Next Step</button>\n    <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"runToEnd()\">Run to end</button>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Reading the finished table</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The answer is always in the <strong>bottom-right cell</strong>:\n  <code>dp[m][n]</code>, where m and n are the lengths of the two strings.\n  The path from bottom-right back to top-left (tracing the minimum choices)\n  tells you exactly which edits were made — a full alignment of the strings.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  For fuzzy search, we only need the number in that final cell. Computing the\n  full path (the <em>alignment</em>) is an optional extra step used when you\n  want to highlight which characters matched.\n</p>\n\n<h2>Complexity</h2>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"margin:1rem 0;\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr><th>Approach</th><th>Time</th><th>Space</th></tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td>Naïve recursion (no memoisation)</td><td>O(3<sup>m</sup>)</td><td>O(m)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>DP table (Wagner–Fischer)</td><td>O(m × n)</td><td>O(m × n)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>DP table, two-row optimised</td><td>O(m × n)</td><td>O(n)</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Space optimisation</span>\n  Each row only needs the previous row's values, so you can discard all but\n  the last two rows. This reduces space from O(m × n) to O(n) — important\n  when scanning many candidates.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. In the DP table, what does <code>dp[0][j]</code> (the entire first row) always equal, and why?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> Always 0 — no edits are needed for empty strings</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Always j — inserting j characters to build B from an empty A</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Always 1 — only one edit is ever needed per row</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> Always the length of B — matching the full string is the base case</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. dp[0][j] = j because converting an empty string to the first j characters of B requires exactly j insertions.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. When filling cell <code>dp[i][j]</code> and A[i] ≠ B[j], the formula is <code>1 + min(dp[i-1][j-1], dp[i-1][j], dp[i][j-1])</code>. Which predecessor corresponds to <em>inserting</em> a character into A?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> dp[i-1][j-1] — the diagonal cell</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> dp[i-1][j]   — the cell directly above</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> dp[i][j-1]   — the cell directly to the left</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> dp[i+1][j+1] — the cell diagonally below-right</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','c','Correct. Moving left means B is one character shorter — equivalent to inserting a character into A to account for that extra character in B.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. Why does dynamic programming reduce the time complexity from exponential to O(m × n)?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> It uses bitwise operations to compare characters faster</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> It avoids recomputing the same subproblem answers by storing them in a table</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> It only computes cells on the diagonal of the table</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> It prunes paths that exceed the threshold before completing them</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. Naïve recursion recomputes the same prefix-pair subproblems exponentially many times. DP stores each answer once and looks it up in O(1), so each of the m×n cells is filled exactly once.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. Where in the completed DP table do you read off the final edit distance?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> The top-left cell dp[0][0]</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> The cell with the smallest value in the table</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> The bottom-right cell dp[m][n]</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> The sum of all values along the main diagonal</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','c','Correct. dp[m][n] holds the edit distance between the full string A (length m) and the full string B (length n).')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://www.baeldung.com/cs/levenshtein-distance-computation\" target=\"_blank\">\n    Levenshtein Distance Computation — Baeldung on Computer Science\n  </a>\n  — Works through the DP table step-by-step with diagrams. Reading this\n  alongside the stepper above will solidify the recurrence relation.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat and I'll explain, rephrase, or go deeper on any cell, step, or formula from this lesson.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0002-edit-distance.html\">← Lesson 2: Edit Distance</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 3 of 6</span>\n  <a href=\"0004-threshold-search.html\">Next: From Distance to Search →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── DP Stepper ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nlet A, B, dp, steps, stepIdx, done;\n\nfunction buildSteps(a, b) {\n  const m = a.length, n = b.length;\n  const table = Array.from({length: m+1}, (_, i) =>\n    Array.from({length: n+1}, (_, j) => i===0 ? j : j===0 ? i : null)\n  );\n  const seq = [];\n  // Emit base-case cells as pre-settled (no explanation needed)\n  for (let i = 1; i <= m; i++)\n    for (let j = 1; j <= n; j++) {\n      const diag = table[i-1][j-1];\n      const top  = table[i-1][j];\n      const left = table[i][j-1];\n      const match = a[i-1] === b[j-1];\n      let val, op;\n      if (match) {\n        val = diag; op = 'match';\n      } else {\n        const best = Math.min(diag, top, left);\n        val = 1 + best;\n        op = best === diag ? 'sub' : best === top ? 'del' : 'ins';\n      }\n      table[i][j] = val;\n      seq.push({i, j, val, op, match, diag, top, left});\n    }\n  return {table, seq};\n}\n\nfunction resetStepper() {\n  A = document.getElementById('str-a').value || 'comit';\n  B = document.getElementById('str-b').value || 'commit';\n  const built = buildSteps(A, B);\n  dp = built.table; steps = built.seq; stepIdx = 0; done = false;\n  renderTable();\n  document.getElementById('step-explanation').innerHTML = 'Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.';\n  document.getElementById('next-btn').disabled = false;\n}\n\nfunction renderTable(highlightStep, showPath) {\n  const m = A.length, n = B.length;\n  const tbl = document.getElementById('stepper-table');\n  let html = '<thead><tr><th></th><th>ε</th>';\n  for (let j = 0; j < n; j++) html += `<th>${B[j]}</th>`;\n  html += '</tr></thead><tbody>';\n  for (let i = 0; i <= m; i++) {\n    html += '<tr>';\n    html += `<th>${i === 0 ? 'ε' : A[i-1]}</th>`;\n    for (let j = 0; j <= n; j++) {\n      const val = dp[i][j];\n      let cls = '';\n      if (showPath && showPath.some(p => p[0]===i && p[1]===j)) cls = 'path';\n      else if (highlightStep) {\n        const {i:ci, j:cj} = highlightStep;\n        if      (i===ci   && j===cj)   cls = 'current';\n        else if (i===ci-1 && j===cj-1) cls = 'used-diag';\n        else if (i===ci-1 && j===cj)   cls = 'used-top';\n        else if (i===ci   && j===cj-1) cls = 'used-left';\n        else if (val !== null && !(i===ci && j===cj)) cls = 'settled';\n      } else if (val !== null) cls = 'settled';\n      const display = val === null ? '·' : val;\n      html += `<td class=\"${cls}\">${display}</td>`;\n    }\n    html += '</tr>';\n  }\n  html += '</tbody>';\n  tbl.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nfunction nextStep() {\n  if (done) return;\n  if (stepIdx >= steps.length) { finishStepper(); return; }\n  const s = steps[stepIdx];\n  // Temporarily null out cells not yet processed\n  for (let k = stepIdx; k < steps.length; k++) {\n    dp[steps[k].i][steps[k].j] = null;\n  }\n  dp[s.i][s.j] = s.val;\n  renderTable(s);\n\n  const ai = A[s.i - 1], bj = B[s.j - 1];\n  let html = '';\n  if (s.match) {\n    html = `<strong>Cell [${s.i},${s.j}]</strong>: A[${s.i}]='<code>${ai}</code>' matches B[${s.j}]='<code>${bj}</code>' — no edit needed. ` +\n           `Carry diagonal: <code>dp[${s.i-1}][${s.j-1}] = ${s.diag}</code> → <strong>${s.val}</strong>`;\n  } else {\n    const ops = [\n      {label:'sub (diagonal)', val:s.diag, cls:'diag', chosen: s.op==='sub'},\n      {label:'del (above)',    val:s.top,  cls:'top',  chosen: s.op==='del'},\n      {label:'ins (left)',     val:s.left, cls:'left', chosen: s.op==='ins'},\n    ];\n    const chosen = ops.find(o => o.chosen);\n    html = `<strong>Cell [${s.i},${s.j}]</strong>: A[${s.i}]='<code>${ai}</code>' ≠ B[${s.j}]='<code>${bj}</code>' — pick cheapest operation + 1.`;\n    html += `<div class=\"op-row\">` + ops.map(o =>\n      `<span class=\"op-badge ${o.cls}${o.chosen ? ' chosen' : ''}\">${o.label}: ${o.val}</span>`\n    ).join('') + `</div>`;\n    html += `<span style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;display:block;\">Chose <strong>${chosen.label}</strong>: 1 + ${chosen.val} = <strong>${s.val}</strong></span>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('step-explanation').innerHTML = html;\n  stepIdx++;\n  if (stepIdx >= steps.length) {\n    document.getElementById('next-btn').textContent = 'Show Path';\n  }\n}\n\nfunction runToEnd() {\n  while (stepIdx < steps.length) {\n    const s = steps[stepIdx];\n    dp[s.i][s.j] = s.val;\n    stepIdx++;\n  }\n  finishStepper();\n}\n\nfunction finishStepper() {\n  done = true;\n  document.getElementById('next-btn').disabled = true;\n  document.getElementById('next-btn').textContent = 'Done';\n  const path = tracePath();\n  renderTable(null, path);\n  const dist = dp[A.length][B.length];\n  document.getElementById('step-explanation').innerHTML =\n    `<strong>Complete.</strong> Edit distance = <strong style=\"font-size:1.2rem;color:var(--success)\">${dist}</strong>. ` +\n    `The green path traces the optimal alignment from bottom-right back to top-left.`;\n}\n\nfunction tracePath() {\n  const path = [];\n  let i = A.length, j = B.length;\n  while (i > 0 || j > 0) {\n    path.push([i, j]);\n    if (i === 0) { j--; continue; }\n    if (j === 0) { i--; continue; }\n    const diag = dp[i-1][j-1], top = dp[i-1][j], left = dp[i][j-1];\n    if (A[i-1] === B[j-1] && dp[i][j] === diag) { i--; j--; }\n    else if (dp[i][j] === 1 + Math.min(diag, top, left)) {\n      const best = Math.min(diag, top, left);\n      if (best === diag) { i--; j--; }\n      else if (best === top) { i--; }\n      else { j--; }\n    }\n  }\n  path.push([0, 0]);\n  return path;\n}\n\n// Init\ndocument.getElementById('str-a').addEventListener('input', resetStepper);\ndocument.getElementById('str-b').addEventListener('input', resetStepper);\nresetStepper();\n\n// ── Quiz logic ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}
```

Input: {
  "file_path": "/work/random/ai-teach-test/lessons/0004-threshold-search.html",
  "content": "<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang=\"en\">\n<head>\n  <meta charset=\"UTF-8\">\n  <meta name=\"viewport\" content=\"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0\">\n  <title>Lesson 4 — From Distance to Search</title>\n  <link rel=\"stylesheet\" href=\"../assets/style.css\">\n  <style>\n    .char-span {\n      display: inline-block;\n      font-family: var(--mono);\n      font-size: 1rem;\n      padding: 0.05em 0.1em;\n      border-radius: 2px;\n    }\n    .char-span.matched {\n      background: #fef9c3;\n      color: #92400e;\n      font-weight: 700;\n    }\n    .threshold-demo { margin: 1.2rem 0; }\n    .threshold-demo label {\n      font-family: var(--sans);\n      font-size: 0.88rem;\n      display: flex;\n      align-items: center;\n      gap: 0.75rem;\n      margin-bottom: 0.5rem;\n    }\n    .threshold-demo input[type=range] { flex: 1; max-width: 200px; }\n    .result-table { width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 0.88rem; margin-top: 0.75rem; }\n    .result-table th { text-align: left; font-family: var(--sans); font-weight: 600; padding: 0.4rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--rule); }\n    .result-table td { padding: 0.35rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--rule); font-family: var(--mono); }\n    .result-table tr.pass td { background: var(--success-bg); }\n    .result-table tr.fail td { color: var(--faint); }\n    .result-table td.dist { text-align: center; }\n    .result-table td.norm { text-align: center; }\n    .verdict { font-weight: 700; }\n    .verdict.yes { color: var(--success); }\n    .verdict.no  { color: var(--danger); }\n    .subseq-input { display: flex; gap: 0.75rem; flex-wrap: wrap; margin-bottom: 0.85rem; }\n    .subseq-input > div { flex: 1; min-width: 130px; }\n    .subseq-input label { font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.78rem; color: var(--muted); display: block; margin-bottom: 0.25rem; }\n    #subseq-visual { font-size: 1.05rem; margin: 0.75rem 0; min-height: 2rem; word-break: break-all; }\n    #subseq-result { font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.9rem; min-height: 1.5rem; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 4 of 6</div>\n  <h1>From Distance to Search</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: choose the right matching model for your query type</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  We can now compute edit distance. But a distance number alone is not a\n  search algorithm. We need to decide: <em>which candidates are matches?</em>\n  And we need to do it fast enough to run on every candidate in a large list.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  This lesson covers two design decisions made at this junction — and one\n  key pivot that explains why tools like fzy and fzf use a <em>different\n  matching model</em> than edit distance entirely.\n</p>\n\n<h2>Approach 1: Fixed threshold k</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The obvious first step: accept a candidate if its edit distance from the\n  query is ≤ k. Choose k based on how permissive you want to be.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo threshold-demo\">\n  <h3>Fixed-threshold demo</h3>\n  <p style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.88rem;color:var(--muted);margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    Query: <code id=\"thresh-query\">cfg</code> — drag the threshold and watch which candidates pass.\n  </p>\n  <label>\n    Threshold k = <strong id=\"k-val\">2</strong>\n    <input type=\"range\" id=\"k-slider\" min=\"0\" max=\"8\" value=\"2\" oninput=\"updateThreshold()\">\n  </label>\n  <table class=\"result-table\" id=\"thresh-table\"></table>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"callout warn\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The problem with fixed k</span>\n  At k=2, <code>cfg.ts</code> (dist 3) is rejected while <code>xx</code> (dist 3 too) passes\n  because it is shorter. The <em>same absolute distance</em> means very different\n  things depending on candidate length. A distance of 3 on a 4-character string\n  is devastating; on a 40-character string it barely matters.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Approach 2: Normalised distance</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Divide the edit distance by the length of the longer string. This gives a\n  similarity ratio between 0 (identical) and 1 (completely different).\n</p>\n\n<pre>normalised_distance(A, B) = edit_distance(A, B) / max(len(A), len(B))</pre>\n\n<p>\n  A threshold of 0.3 means \"accept if fewer than 30% of characters differ.\"\n  This scales gracefully with string length.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Better, but not sufficient</span>\n  Normalised distance solves the length problem for typo-style queries.\n  But it still fails for abbreviation queries like <code>authcfg</code> →\n  <code>auth_config_loader.ts</code>, where edit distance is large (11)\n  but the user's intent is obvious. The characters are all there — just\n  not contiguous.\n</div>\n\n<h2>The pivot: subsequence matching</h2>\n\n<p>\n  This is the key insight behind fzy, fzf, and most modern command-palette\n  and file-finder tools:\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  For interactive file/command search, the user is almost always\n  <em>abbreviating</em>, not misspelling. They type the first letters of\n  words, or the distinctive characters. The right matching model is\n  therefore <strong>subsequence matching</strong> — not edit distance.\n  <br><br>\n  A query Q is a <strong>subsequence</strong> of candidate C if all characters\n  of Q appear in C in the same order (but not necessarily contiguously).\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  This is a stricter gate than edit distance in one sense (you must have\n  all characters, in order) but far more permissive in another (gaps are\n  free — you can skip any number of characters in the candidate).\n</p>\n\n<h3>Why subsequence beats edit distance for this use case</h3>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"margin:1rem 0;width:100%\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr><th>Query</th><th>Candidate</th><th>Edit dist</th><th>Subsequence?</th><th>Is it a match?</th></tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td><code>authcfg</code></td><td><code>auth_config_loader.ts</code></td><td>13</td><td>✓ yes</td><td>Yes — user abbreviated</td></tr>\n    <tr><td><code>MC</code></td><td><code>MyComponent.tsx</code></td><td>13</td><td>✓ yes</td><td>Yes — initials</td></tr>\n    <tr><td><code>comit</code></td><td><code>commit</code></td><td>1</td><td>✓ yes</td><td>Yes — typo</td></tr>\n    <tr><td><code>xqz</code></td><td><code>commit</code></td><td>6</td><td>✗ no</td><td>No — random characters</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<p>\n  Edit distance gives large, meaningless numbers for abbreviation queries.\n  Subsequence gives a clean binary: either all your characters are present\n  in order, or they aren't.\n</p>\n\n<h2>The subsequence check algorithm</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Checking whether Q is a subsequence of C is a simple greedy scan in\n  O(|C|) time — much faster than the O(|Q| × |C|) DP table:\n</p>\n\n<pre>function isSubsequence(query, candidate):\n  qi = 0                       // pointer into query\n  for each character c in candidate:\n    if c == query[qi]:\n      qi++                     // advance query pointer on match\n    if qi == query.length:\n      return true              // all query chars found in order\n  return false                 // ran out of candidate chars</pre>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why this matters for performance</span>\n  In a fuzzy finder scanning thousands of filenames, the subsequence check\n  runs first. Only candidates that pass it proceed to the expensive scoring\n  step. Most candidates are eliminated in O(n) time, making the overall\n  system feel instant.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Try it: Subsequence finder</h2>\n\n<div class=\"demo\">\n  <h3>Is query a subsequence of candidate?</h3>\n  <div class=\"subseq-input\">\n    <div>\n      <label>Query</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sq-query\" value=\"authcfg\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div>\n      <label>Candidate</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sq-candidate\" value=\"auth_config_loader.ts\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div id=\"subseq-visual\"></div>\n  <div id=\"subseq-result\"></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The complete matching pipeline</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Putting it together, here is the pipeline that fzy-style tools use:\n</p>\n\n<ol>\n  <li>\n    <strong>Subsequence gate</strong> (O(n) per candidate) — if the query\n    is not a subsequence of the candidate, reject immediately. No score computed.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <strong>Score</strong> (O(|Q| × |C|) per surviving candidate) — run the\n    scoring DP to assign a rank. This is what Lesson 5 covers.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <strong>Sort by score</strong> — the highest-scoring candidate is the\n    top result.\n  </li>\n</ol>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The key shift</span>\n  fzy does not use edit distance at all. The subsequence check replaces\n  the threshold step entirely. The scoring model (next lesson) replaces the\n  \"which edit is cheapest?\" question with \"which match position feels most\n  intentional?\"\n</div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. Is <code>usr</code> a subsequence of <code>usr_config.ts</code>?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> No — usr does not appear as a contiguous substring</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Yes — u, s, r all appear in order at positions 0, 1, 2</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Only if edit distance is less than 3</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> No — subsequence requires exact contiguous matching</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. u-s-r appear at the very start of usr_config.ts in order. Gaps are free in subsequence matching — contiguity is not required.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. Why is the subsequence check run <em>before</em> the scoring DP in fzy's pipeline?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> Because scoring requires the subsequence positions as input</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> Because it eliminates non-matches cheaply in O(n), avoiding the costly O(mn) scoring step</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> Because subsequence distance is more accurate than the scoring model</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> Because it converts the query to lowercase before scoring begins</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. The subsequence check is O(n) — very cheap. It eliminates the majority of candidates before the O(mn) scoring DP runs, keeping the system fast.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. What is the fundamental reason why edit distance is a poor matching model for abbreviation queries like <code>MC</code> → <code>MyComponent.tsx</code>?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> Edit distance is too slow to compute for short queries</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> Edit distance penalises gaps between matched characters, making abbreviations appear far away</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> Edit distance requires both strings to be the same length</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> Edit distance cannot handle uppercase letters</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. To go from MC to MyComponent.tsx by edits, you need many insertions — one for every skipped character. Subsequence matching treats those gaps as free, which better models the user\\'s intent.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. In fzy's pipeline, after a candidate passes the subsequence gate, what determines its final rank in the results?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> Its edit distance from the query</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> The alphabetical order of the candidate string</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> A scoring model that rewards compact and boundary-aligned matches</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> The length of the candidate — shorter candidates always rank higher</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','c','Correct. The scoring model is what Lesson 5 covers. It assigns higher scores to matches that are consecutive, start at word/path boundaries, and are compact relative to candidate length.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://github.com/jhawthorn/fzy/blob/master/ALGORITHM.md\" target=\"_blank\">\n    fzy ALGORITHM.md — jhawthorn (GitHub)\n  </a>\n  — Read the opening paragraphs up through \"Scoring.\" It describes exactly\n  the pipeline covered in this lesson: subsequence gate first, then a scoring\n  DP. This is the document you will fully understand by the end of Lesson 5.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat and I'll explain, rephrase, or go deeper on anything from this lesson.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0003-dp-table.html\">← Lesson 3: The DP Table</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 4 of 6</span>\n  <a href=\"0005-scoring-model.html\">Next: The Scoring Model →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── Threshold demo ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction editDistance(a, b) {\n  const m = a.length, n = b.length;\n  const dp = Array.from({length: m+1}, (_, i) =>\n    Array.from({length: n+1}, (_, j) => i===0 ? j : j===0 ? i : 0)\n  );\n  for (let i = 1; i <= m; i++)\n    for (let j = 1; j <= n; j++) {\n      if (a[i-1] === b[j-1]) dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j-1];\n      else dp[i][j] = 1 + Math.min(dp[i-1][j-1], dp[i-1][j], dp[i][j-1]);\n    }\n  return dp[m][n];\n}\n\nconst CANDIDATES = [\n  'cfg.ts',\n  'config.json',\n  'auth_config_loader.ts',\n  'package.json',\n  'xx',\n  'cfg',\n  'app_configuration_manager.ts',\n  'index.ts',\n];\n\nconst QUERY = 'cfg';\n\nfunction updateThreshold() {\n  const k = parseInt(document.getElementById('k-slider').value);\n  document.getElementById('k-val').textContent = k;\n  const rows = CANDIDATES.map(c => {\n    const d = editDistance(QUERY, c.toLowerCase());\n    const norm = (d / Math.max(QUERY.length, c.length)).toFixed(2);\n    const pass = d <= k;\n    return `<tr class=\"${pass ? 'pass' : 'fail'}\">\n      <td>${c}</td>\n      <td class=\"dist\">${d}</td>\n      <td class=\"norm\">${norm}</td>\n      <td class=\"verdict ${pass ? 'yes' : 'no'}\">${pass ? '✓ match' : '✗ reject'}</td>\n    </tr>`;\n  });\n  document.getElementById('thresh-table').innerHTML = `\n    <thead><tr><th>Candidate</th><th>Edit dist</th><th>Normalised</th><th>Result (k=${k})</th></tr></thead>\n    <tbody>${rows.join('')}</tbody>`;\n}\nupdateThreshold();\n\n// ── Subsequence finder ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction findSubseq(query, candidate) {\n  const q = query.toLowerCase();\n  const c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  const positions = [];\n  let qi = 0;\n  for (let ci = 0; ci < c.length && qi < q.length; ci++) {\n    if (c[ci] === q[qi]) { positions.push(ci); qi++; }\n  }\n  return qi === q.length ? positions : null;\n}\n\nfunction updateSubseq() {\n  const query     = document.getElementById('sq-query').value;\n  const candidate = document.getElementById('sq-candidate').value;\n  const visual    = document.getElementById('subseq-visual');\n  const result    = document.getElementById('subseq-result');\n\n  if (!query || !candidate) { visual.innerHTML = ''; result.textContent = ''; return; }\n\n  const positions = findSubseq(query, candidate);\n\n  const spans = candidate.split('').map((ch, i) => {\n    const cls = positions && positions.includes(i) ? 'char-span matched' : 'char-span';\n    return `<span class=\"${cls}\">${ch === ' ' ? '&nbsp;' : ch}</span>`;\n  }).join('');\n  visual.innerHTML = spans;\n\n  if (positions) {\n    result.innerHTML = `<span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;\">✓ Subsequence match</span>\n      — all ${query.length} query characters found in order (highlighted).`;\n  } else {\n    result.innerHTML = `<span style=\"color:var(--danger);font-weight:700;\">✗ Not a subsequence</span>\n      — not all query characters appear in order in the candidate.`;\n  }\n}\n\ndocument.getElementById('sq-query').addEventListener('input', updateSubseq);\ndocument.getElementById('sq-candidate').addEventListener('input', updateSubseq);\nupdateSubseq();\n\n// ── Quiz logic ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}

  "command": "xdg-open /work/random/ai-teach-test/lessons/0004-threshold-search.html 2>/dev/null || echo \"open manually: /work/random/ai-teach-test/lessons/0004-threshold-search.html\"",

Opening in existing browser session.

Lesson 4 is open. This one contains an important pivot — probably the most conceptually surprising moment in the course.

**The arc of the lesson:**

1. **Fixed threshold k** — drag the slider and watch the table. You'll immediately see the problem: a distance of 3 means something totally different on a 4-character string vs a 40-character string.

2. **Normalised distance** — divide by max length to get a 0–1 ratio. Better, but still broken for abbreviations: `authcfg` → `auth_config_loader.ts` has edit distance 13, making it look like a terrible match.

3. **The pivot** — fzy and fzf don't use edit distance for matching at all. They use **subsequence matching**. The query characters just need to appear in order; gaps between them are free. This is the correct model for how humans actually abbreviate.

4. **The subsequence check demo** — type any query and candidate, watch matched characters highlight in yellow.

**The key takeaway**: edit distance and subsequence are solving different problems. Edit distance models "how many typos?" Subsequence models "did the user pick the right characters?" For interactive search, the second question is almost always the right one.

Once you're done, come back and I'll build Lesson 5 — the scoring model that answers "given that Q is a subsequence of C, which position of the match is most intentional?"

**Tool:** `Write`

}\n    .result-table tr.fail td { color: var(--faint); }\n    .result-table td.dist { text-align: center; }\n    .result-table td.norm { text-align: center; }\n    .verdict { font-weight: 700; }\n    .verdict.yes { color: var(--success); }\n    .verdict.no  { color: var(--danger); }\n    .subseq-input { display: flex; gap: 0.75rem; flex-wrap: wrap; margin-bottom: 0.85rem; }\n    .subseq-input > div { flex: 1; min-width: 130px; }\n    .subseq-input label { font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.78rem; color: var(--muted); display: block; margin-bottom: 0.25rem; }\n    #subseq-visual { font-size: 1.05rem; margin: 0.75rem 0; min-height: 2rem; word-break: break-all; }\n    #subseq-result { font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.9rem; min-height: 1.5rem; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 4 of 6</div>\n  <h1>From Distance to Search</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: choose the right matching model for your query type</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  We can now compute edit distance. But a distance number alone is not a\n  search algorithm. We need to decide: <em>which candidates are matches?</em>\n  And we need to do it fast enough to run on every candidate in a large list.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  This lesson covers two design decisions made at this junction — and one\n  key pivot that explains why tools like fzy and fzf use a <em>different\n  matching model</em> than edit distance entirely.\n</p>\n\n<h2>Approach 1: Fixed threshold k</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The obvious first step: accept a candidate if its edit distance from the\n  query is ≤ k. Choose k based on how permissive you want to be.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo threshold-demo\">\n  <h3>Fixed-threshold demo</h3>\n  <p style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.88rem;color:var(--muted);margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    Query: <code id=\"thresh-query\">cfg</code> — drag the threshold and watch which candidates pass.\n  </p>\n  <label>\n    Threshold k = <strong id=\"k-val\">2</strong>\n    <input type=\"range\" id=\"k-slider\" min=\"0\" max=\"8\" value=\"2\" oninput=\"updateThreshold()\">\n  </label>\n  <table class=\"result-table\" id=\"thresh-table\"></table>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"callout warn\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The problem with fixed k</span>\n  At k=2, <code>cfg.ts</code> (dist 3) is rejected while <code>xx</code> (dist 3 too) passes\n  because it is shorter. The <em>same absolute distance</em> means very different\n  things depending on candidate length. A distance of 3 on a 4-character string\n  is devastating; on a 40-character string it barely matters.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Approach 2: Normalised distance</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Divide the edit distance by the length of the longer string. This gives a\n  similarity ratio between 0 (identical) and 1 (completely different).\n</p>\n\n<pre>normalised_distance(A, B) = edit_distance(A, B) / max(len(A), len(B))</pre>\n\n<p>\n  A threshold of 0.3 means \"accept if fewer than 30% of characters differ.\"\n  This scales gracefully with string length.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Better, but not sufficient</span>\n  Normalised distance solves the length problem for typo-style queries.\n  But it still fails for abbreviation queries like <code>authcfg</code> →\n  <code>auth_config_loader.ts</code>, where edit distance is large (11)\n  but the user's intent is obvious. The characters are all there — just\n  not contiguous.\n</div>\n\n<h2>The pivot: subsequence matching</h2>\n\n<p>\n  This is the key insight behind fzy, fzf, and most modern command-palette\n  and file-finder tools:\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  For interactive file/command search, the user is almost always\n  <em>abbreviating</em>, not misspelling. They type the first letters of\n  words, or the distinctive characters. The right matching model is\n  therefore <strong>subsequence matching</strong> — not edit distance.\n  <br><br>\n  A query Q is a <strong>subsequence</strong> of candidate C if all characters\n  of Q appear in C in the same order (but not necessarily contiguously).\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  This is a stricter gate than edit distance in one sense (you must have\n  all characters, in order) but far more permissive in another (gaps are\n  free — you can skip any number of characters in the candidate).\n</p>\n\n<h3>Why subsequence beats edit distance for this use case</h3>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"margin:1rem 0;width:100%\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr><th>Query</th><th>Candidate</th><th>Edit dist</th><th>Subsequence?</th><th>Is it a match?</th></tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td><code>authcfg</code></td><td><code>auth_config_loader.ts</code></td><td>13</td><td>✓ yes</td><td>Yes — user abbreviated</td></tr>\n    <tr><td><code>MC</code></td><td><code>MyComponent.tsx</code></td><td>13</td><td>✓ yes</td><td>Yes — initials</td></tr>\n    <tr><td><code>comit</code></td><td><code>commit</code></td><td>1</td><td>✓ yes</td><td>Yes — typo</td></tr>\n    <tr><td><code>xqz</code></td><td><code>commit</code></td><td>6</td><td>✗ no</td><td>No — random characters</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<p>\n  Edit distance gives large, meaningless numbers for abbreviation queries.\n  Subsequence gives a clean binary: either all your characters are present\n  in order, or they aren't.\n</p>\n\n<h2>The subsequence check algorithm</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Checking whether Q is a subsequence of C is a simple greedy scan in\n  O(|C|) time — much faster than the O(|Q| × |C|) DP table:\n</p>\n\n<pre>function isSubsequence(query, candidate):\n  qi = 0                       // pointer into query\n  for each character c in candidate:\n    if c == query[qi]:\n      qi++                     // advance query pointer on match\n    if qi == query.length:\n      return true              // all query chars found in order\n  return false                 // ran out of candidate chars</pre>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why this matters for performance</span>\n  In a fuzzy finder scanning thousands of filenames, the subsequence check\n  runs first. Only candidates that pass it proceed to the expensive scoring\n  step. Most candidates are eliminated in O(n) time, making the overall\n  system feel instant.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Try it: Subsequence finder</h2>\n\n<div class=\"demo\">\n  <h3>Is query a subsequence of candidate?</h3>\n  <div class=\"subseq-input\">\n    <div>\n      <label>Query</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sq-query\" value=\"authcfg\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div>\n      <label>Candidate</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sq-candidate\" value=\"auth_config_loader.ts\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div id=\"subseq-visual\"></div>\n  <div id=\"subseq-result\"></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The complete matching pipeline</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Putting it together, here is the pipeline that fzy-style tools use:\n</p>\n\n<ol>\n  <li>\n    <strong>Subsequence gate</strong> (O(n) per candidate) — if the query\n    is not a subsequence of the candidate, reject immediately. No score computed.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <strong>Score</strong> (O(|Q| × |C|) per surviving candidate) — run the\n    scoring DP to assign a rank. This is what Lesson 5 covers.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <strong>Sort by score</strong> — the highest-scoring candidate is the\n    top result.\n  </li>\n</ol>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The key shift</span>\n  fzy does not use edit distance at all. The subsequence check replaces\n  the threshold step entirely. The scoring model (next lesson) replaces the\n  \"which edit is cheapest?\" question with \"which match position feels most\n  intentional?\"\n</div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. Is <code>usr</code> a subsequence of <code>usr_config.ts</code>?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> No — usr does not appear as a contiguous substring</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Yes — u, s, r all appear in order at positions 0, 1, 2</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Only if edit distance is less than 3</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> No — subsequence requires exact contiguous matching</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. u-s-r appear at the very start of usr_config.ts in order. Gaps are free in subsequence matching — contiguity is not required.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. Why is the subsequence check run <em>before</em> the scoring DP in fzy's pipeline?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> Because scoring requires the subsequence positions as input</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> Because it eliminates non-matches cheaply in O(n), avoiding the costly O(mn) scoring step</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> Because subsequence distance is more accurate than the scoring model</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> Because it converts the query to lowercase before scoring begins</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. The subsequence check is O(n) — very cheap. It eliminates the majority of candidates before the O(mn) scoring DP runs, keeping the system fast.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. What is the fundamental reason why edit distance is a poor matching model for abbreviation queries like <code>MC</code> → <code>MyComponent.tsx</code>?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> Edit distance is too slow to compute for short queries</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> Edit distance penalises gaps between matched characters, making abbreviations appear far away</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> Edit distance requires both strings to be the same length</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> Edit distance cannot handle uppercase letters</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. To go from MC to MyComponent.tsx by edits, you need many insertions — one for every skipped character. Subsequence matching treats those gaps as free, which better models the user\\'s intent.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. In fzy's pipeline, after a candidate passes the subsequence gate, what determines its final rank in the results?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> Its edit distance from the query</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> The alphabetical order of the candidate string</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> A scoring model that rewards compact and boundary-aligned matches</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> The length of the candidate — shorter candidates always rank higher</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','c','Correct. The scoring model is what Lesson 5 covers. It assigns higher scores to matches that are consecutive, start at word/path boundaries, and are compact relative to candidate length.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://github.com/jhawthorn/fzy/blob/master/ALGORITHM.md\" target=\"_blank\">\n    fzy ALGORITHM.md — jhawthorn (GitHub)\n  </a>\n  — Read the opening paragraphs up through \"Scoring.\" It describes exactly\n  the pipeline covered in this lesson: subsequence gate first, then a scoring\n  DP. This is the document you will fully understand by the end of Lesson 5.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat and I'll explain, rephrase, or go deeper on anything from this lesson.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0003-dp-table.html\">← Lesson 3: The DP Table</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 4 of 6</span>\n  <a href=\"0005-scoring-model.html\">Next: The Scoring Model →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── Threshold demo ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction editDistance(a, b) {\n  const m = a.length, n = b.length;\n  const dp = Array.from({length: m+1}, (_, i) =>\n    Array.from({length: n+1}, (_, j) => i===0 ? j : j===0 ? i : 0)\n  );\n  for (let i = 1; i <= m; i++)\n    for (let j = 1; j <= n; j++) {\n      if (a[i-1] === b[j-1]) dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j-1];\n      else dp[i][j] = 1 + Math.min(dp[i-1][j-1], dp[i-1][j], dp[i][j-1]);\n    }\n  return dp[m][n];\n}\n\nconst CANDIDATES = [\n  'cfg.ts',\n  'config.json',\n  'auth_config_loader.ts',\n  'package.json',\n  'xx',\n  'cfg',\n  'app_configuration_manager.ts',\n  'index.ts',\n];\n\nconst QUERY = 'cfg';\n\nfunction updateThreshold() {\n  const k = parseInt(document.getElementById('k-slider').value);\n  document.getElementById('k-val').textContent = k;\n  const rows = CANDIDATES.map(c => {\n    const d = editDistance(QUERY, c.toLowerCase());\n    const norm = (d / Math.max(QUERY.length, c.length)).toFixed(2);\n    const pass = d <= k;\n    return `<tr class=\"${pass ? 'pass' : 'fail'}\">\n      <td>${c}</td>\n      <td class=\"dist\">${d}</td>\n      <td class=\"norm\">${norm}</td>\n      <td class=\"verdict ${pass ? 'yes' : 'no'}\">${pass ? '✓ match' : '✗ reject'}</td>\n    </tr>`;\n  });\n  document.getElementById('thresh-table').innerHTML = `\n    <thead><tr><th>Candidate</th><th>Edit dist</th><th>Normalised</th><th>Result (k=${k})</th></tr></thead>\n    <tbody>${rows.join('')}</tbody>`;\n}\nupdateThreshold();\n\n// ── Subsequence finder ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction findSubseq(query, candidate) {\n  const q = query.toLowerCase();\n  const c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  const positions = [];\n  let qi = 0;\n  for (let ci = 0; ci < c.length && qi < q.length; ci++) {\n    if (c[ci] === q[qi]) { positions.push(ci); qi++; }\n  }\n  return qi === q.length ? positions : null;\n}\n\nfunction updateSubseq() {\n  const query     = document.getElementById('sq-query').value;\n  const candidate = document.getElementById('sq-candidate').value;\n  const visual    = document.getElementById('subseq-visual');\n  const result    = document.getElementById('subseq-result');\n\n  if (!query || !candidate) { visual.innerHTML = ''; result.textContent = ''; return; }\n\n  const positions = findSubseq(query, candidate);\n\n  const spans = candidate.split('').map((ch, i) => {\n    const cls = positions && positions.includes(i) ? 'char-span matched' : 'char-span';\n    return `<span class=\"${cls}\">${ch === ' ' ? '&nbsp;' : ch}</span>`;\n  }).join('');\n  visual.innerHTML = spans;\n\n  if (positions) {\n    result.innerHTML = `<span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;\">✓ Subsequence match</span>\n      — all ${query.length} query characters found in order (highlighted).`;\n  } else {\n    result.innerHTML = `<span style=\"color:var(--danger);font-weight:700;\">✗ Not a subsequence</span>\n      — not all query characters appear in order in the candidate.`;\n  }\n}\n\ndocument.getElementById('sq-query').addEventListener('input', updateSubseq);\ndocument.getElementById('sq-candidate').addEventListener('input', updateSubseq);\nupdateSubseq();\n\n// ── Quiz logic ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}
```
