background: #fafafa;\n    }\n    .comp-card.winner { border-color: var(--success); background: var(--success-bg); }\n    .comp-card .label {\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.75rem; font-weight: 700;\n      text-transform: uppercase; letter-spacing: 0.07em;\n      color: var(--muted); margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\n    }\n    .comp-card.winner .label { color: var(--success); }\n    .comp-score { font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 1.1rem; font-weight: 700; }\n\n    .bonus-table { width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 0.88rem; margin: 1rem 0; }\n    .bonus-table th { text-align: left; font-family: var(--sans); font-weight: 600;\n      padding: 0.4rem 0.6rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--rule); }\n    .bonus-table td { padding: 0.35rem 0.6rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--rule); font-family: var(--mono); }\n    .bonus-table td:last-child { font-weight: 700; }\n\n    .score-legend { display: flex; gap: 0.9rem; flex-wrap: wrap;\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.8rem; margin: 0.5rem 0 1rem; }\n    .score-legend span { display: flex; align-items: center; word-break: break-all; min-height: 2rem; margin: 0.5rem 0; line-height: 1.9; }\n    #live-breakdown { font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.88rem; margin-top: 0.5rem; }\n    #live-total { font-size: 1.2rem; font-weight: 700; font-family: var(--mono); color: var(--accent); }\n    .breakdown-row { display: flex; justify-content: space-between;\n      border-bottom: 1px solid var(--rule); padding: 0.22rem 0; font-size: 0.85rem; }\n    .breakdown-row:last-child { border-bottom: none; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5 of 6</div>\n  <h1>The Scoring Model</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: rank matches by intent, not just by existence</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  After the subsequence gate (Lesson 4), we know a query's characters all\n  appear in the candidate in order. But a query like <code>cfg</code> matches\n  <code>cfg.ts</code> and <code>app_configuration_manager.ts</code> equally\n  — both are valid subsequences. How do we know which one the user meant?\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  Assign each match a <strong>score</strong> based on the quality of the\n  alignment, not just its existence. The scoring model encodes human\n  intuitions about intentionality: <em>consecutive runs are more deliberate\n  than scattered letters; matching word starts shows structural awareness;\n  compact matches in short strings are more precise.</em>\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  This is the heart of fzy's algorithm. Every design decision in the scoring\n  model solves one specific failure of naive subsequence matching.\n</p>\n\n<h2>The three scoring decisions</h2>\n\n<h3>Decision 1 — Consecutive match bonus</h3>\n\n<p>\n  If matched characters run consecutively in the candidate, the user almost\n  certainly typed exactly that substring. Award a large bonus per consecutive\n  pair.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"comparison-grid\">\n  <div class=\"comp-card\">\n    <div class=\"label\">Scattered match</div>\n    <div class=\"candidate-line\">\n      <span class=\"ch m-plain\">c</span>on<span class=\"ch gap-inner\">f</span>i<span class=\"ch gap-inner\">g</span>uration\n    </div>\n    <div>query <code>cfg</code> matched to positions 0, 3, 5 — gaps between every char</div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"comp-card winner\">\n    <div class=\"label\">Consecutive match ✓ wins</div>\n    <div class=\"candidate-line\">\n      <span class=\"ch m-boundary\">c</span><span class=\"ch m-consec\">f</span><span class=\"ch m-consec\">g</span>.ts\n    </div>\n    <div>query <code>cfg</code> matched to positions 0, 1, 2 — three consecutive characters</div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h3>Decision 2 — Word boundary bonus</h3>\n\n<p>\n  Matching the first character of a word (after <code>/</code>, <code>_</code>,\n  <code>-</code>, space, <code>.</code>, or uppercase-after-lowercase) means\n  the user is thinking in terms of structure, not raw characters.\n  Award a bonus scaled by boundary type.\n</p>\n\n<table class=\"bonus-table\">\n  <thead><tr><th>Boundary type</th><th>Example trigger</th><th>Bonus</th></tr></thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td>Path separator <code>/</code></td><td><code>/usr/<strong>l</strong>ocal</code></td><td>+0.9</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Word char <code>_ - space</code></td><td><code>auth_<strong>c</strong>onfig</code></td><td>+0.8</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>camelCase capital</td><td><code>my<strong>C</strong>omponent</code></td><td>+0.8</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Dot separator</td><td><code>index.<strong>t</strong>s</code></td><td>+0.6</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>No boundary</td><td><code>con<strong>f</strong>ig</code></td><td>+0.0</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why these values?</span>\n  Path separators rank highest because typing <code>usr/l</code> precisely signals\n  you want something <em>inside</em> <code>/usr/</code>. Word chars are next —\n  they show you know the token structure. Mid-word matches are penalised\n  because they could easily be accidental.\n</div>\n\n<h3>Decision 3 — Gap penalty (affine)</h3>\n\n<p>\n  Every unmatched character between two matched characters is a \"gap.\"\n  Gaps are penalised because they suggest the match was accidental.\n  fzy uses an <strong>affine gap penalty</strong>: a fixed cost for\n  <em>opening</em> a gap, plus a smaller cost per additional character in it.\n</p>\n\n<pre>gap_cost(length) = GAP_OPEN + (length - 1) × GAP_EXTEND\n\nwhere: GAP_OPEN = -0.01   (per character, inner gaps)\n       Outer gaps (leading/trailing) = -0.005 per character</pre>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why affine and not linear?</span>\n  Borrowed from bioinformatics (Gotoh, 1982). A single long gap is more\n  \"forgivable\" than many short gaps: one long skip might just mean the\n  file has a long suffix. Many small gaps suggest the match is scattered\n  by coincidence. Affine penalties encode this by making the first character\n  of a gap more expensive than subsequent ones.\n</div>\n\n<h2>The two-matrix DP</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The scoring DP builds two matrices over the same (query × candidate) grid:\n</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <strong>M[i][j]</strong> — the best score for matching the first <code>i</code>\n    query characters to the first <code>j</code> candidate characters,\n    with query[i] matched to candidate[j]. May have arrived here via a gap.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <strong>D[i][j]</strong> — the same, but <em>query[i] is part of a\n    consecutive run</em> (no gap before this match). Used to compute the\n    consecutive bonus correctly.\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<pre>// Bonus at candidate position j\nB[j] = boundary_bonus(candidate, j)\n\n// D: consecutive-run score ending at (i, j)\nD[i][j] = max(\n  M[i-1][j-1] + CONSECUTIVE + B[j],   // extend a run from any previous match\n  D[i-1][j-1] + CONSECUTIVE + B[j]    // extend a confirmed consecutive run\n)\n\n// M: best score overall ending at (i, j)\nM[i][j] = max(\n  D[i][j],                             // end a consecutive run here\n  best over k < j: M[i-1][k] + gap_cost(j - k) + B[j]\n)</pre>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why two matrices?</span>\n  The consecutive bonus applies when <em>both</em> the previous and current\n  query characters are matched without a gap. If you tracked only one matrix\n  you couldn't distinguish \"I arrived here from a consecutive run\" from\n  \"I arrived here via a gap.\" The D matrix carries that information.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Live scorer</h2>\n\n<p>Type a query and candidate to see the fzy-style score and alignment.</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\">\n  <h3>Scoring explorer</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:120px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Query</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sc-query\" value=\"cfg\" maxlength=\"12\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:2;min-width:200px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Candidate</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sc-candidate\" value=\"auth_config_loader.ts\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"score-legend\">\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#dcfce7;border-color:#16a34a;\"></span> Consecutive match</span>\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#dbeafe;border-color:#3b82f6;\"></span> Boundary match</span>\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#fef9c3;border-color:#ca8a04;\"></span> Plain match</span>\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#fee2e2;border-color:#dc2626;\"></span> Inner gap</span>\n  </div>\n  <div id=\"live-candidate\" class=\"candidate-line\"></div>\n  <div id=\"live-breakdown\"></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Seeing the ranking in action</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Below are four candidates for query <code>cfg</code>, ranked by their\n  fzy score. Hover over each to see why it ranks where it does.\n</p>\n\n<div id=\"ranking-demo\"></div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. Query <code>mc</code> against <code>MyComponent.tsx</code>. The M matches at position 0 (capital, start of string) and the C at position 2 (camelCase capital). What type of bonus applies to both?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> Consecutive match bonus — the characters run one after another</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Boundary bonus — both M and C are at camelCase word boundaries</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Gap penalty — there is one character between M and C</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> Path separator bonus — the file extension creates a boundary</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. M is at position 0 (start of string = highest boundary bonus), C is a capital after lowercase (camelCase boundary). Both earn +0.8 or higher.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. Why does fzy use an <em>affine</em> gap penalty rather than a flat penalty per gap character?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> To make the score always a negative number</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> One long gap is more forgivable than many short gaps — affine makes opening a gap cost more than extending it</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> To ensure the score is comparable across strings of different lengths</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> Affine penalties are faster to compute than linear ones</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. Many short gaps suggest scattered/accidental matching. One long gap might just be a long file suffix. Affine penalty encodes this: pay more to open a gap, less to extend an existing one.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. The scoring DP uses two matrices: M and D. What specifically does the D matrix track that M alone cannot?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> Whether the current match character is uppercase</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> The best score where the current match is part of a consecutive run (no gap before it)</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> The cumulative gap penalty across the entire candidate</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> The minimum number of gaps needed to complete the match</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. D[i][j] tracks the score when query[i] arrived at candidate[j] without a gap from the previous match. This is needed to correctly apply the consecutive bonus, which only fires when both the current and previous matches were adjacent.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. Query <code>ts</code>. Candidate A: <code>tools.ts</code> (matches <code>t</code> at position 0, <code>s</code> at position 7 after the dot). Candidate B: <code>timestamp.js</code> (matches <code>t</code> at 0, <code>s</code> at 4 consecutively as part of \"times\"). Which scores higher and why?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> A scores higher — the dot before .ts is a boundary, giving a large bonus to s</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> B scores higher — ts appears consecutively near the start with no gap bonus needed</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> They score equally — both match t at position 0</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> A scores higher — shorter strings always rank above longer ones</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','a','Correct. In tools.ts the s matches after a dot boundary (+0.6) and t matches at position 0. This is the intended match — the user typed ts to find TypeScript files. The dot-boundary bonus on s elevates it above a mid-word consecutive match with no boundary signal.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://github.com/jhawthorn/fzy/blob/master/ALGORITHM.md\" target=\"_blank\">\n    fzy ALGORITHM.md — jhawthorn (GitHub)\n  </a>\n  — You now have everything you need to read this document end-to-end and\n  understand every paragraph. Read it now: the gap score, the bonus values,\n  the two-matrix DP, and the rationale for each constant.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat and I'll go deeper on any scoring decision, matrix cell, or constant from this lesson.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0004-threshold-search.html\">← Lesson 4: From Distance to Search</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5 of 6</span>\n  <a href=\"0006-bitap.html\">Next: The Bitap Algorithm →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── Scoring constants (fzy-faithful) ─────────────────────────────────────────\nconst SCORE_GAP_LEADING    = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_TRAILING   = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_INNER      = -0.01;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE = 1.0;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_SLASH    = 0.9;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_WORD     = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL  = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_DOT      = 0.6;\nconst SCORE_MIN            = -Infinity;\n\nfunction charBonus(str, i) {\n  if (i === 0) return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  const prev = str[i - 1], cur = str[i];\n  if (prev === '/' || prev === '\\\\') return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  if (prev === '_' || prev === '-' || prev === ' ') return SCORE_MATCH_WORD;\n  if (prev === '.') return SCORE_MATCH_DOT;\n  if (cur >= 'A' && cur <= 'Z' && prev >= 'a' && prev <= 'z') return SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL;\n  return 0;\n}\n\nfunction isSubseq(query, candidate) {\n  const q = query.toLowerCase(), c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  let qi = 0;\n  for (let ci = 0; ci < c.length && qi < q.length; ci++)\n    if (c[ci] === q[qi]) qi++;\n  return qi === q.length;\n}\n\nfunction score(query, candidate) {\n  const n = query.length, m = candidate.length;\n  const q = query.toLowerCase(), c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  if (!isSubseq(q, c)) return { score: SCORE_MIN, positions: [] };\n\n  // Precompute bonuses\n  const bonus = Array.from({length: m}, (_, i) => charBonus(candidate, i));\n\n  // Two matrices: D (consecutive), M (best overall)\n  // Initialise with -Infinity\n  const D = Array.from({length: n}, () => new Float64Array(m).fill(SCORE_MIN));\n  const M = Array.from({length: n}, () => new Float64Array(m).fill(SCORE_MIN));\n\n  for (let i = 0; i < n; i++) {\n    let prevScore = SCORE_MIN;\n    const gapScore = i === n - 1 ? SCORE_GAP_TRAILING : SCORE_GAP_INNER;\n\n    for (let j = (i === 0 ? 0 : i); j < m; j++) {\n      if (q[i] === c[j]) {\n        let bScore = bonus[j];\n        if (i === 0) {\n          // First query char: leading gap from start\n          const leadGap = j * SCORE_GAP_LEADING;\n          D[i][j] = leadGap + bScore;\n          M[i][j] = D[i][j];\n        } else {\n          // D: consecutive from previous query char at j-1\n          const dVal = j > 0 && D[i-1][j-1] > SCORE_MIN\n            ? D[i-1][j-1] + SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE + bScore\n            : SCORE_MIN;\n          // Also: M from j-1 + consecutive (extending any match)\n          const mVal = j > 0 && M[i-1][j-1] > SCORE_MIN\n            ? M[i-1][j-1] + SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE + bScore\n            : SCORE_MIN;\n          D[i][j] = Math.max(dVal, mVal);\n          M[i][j] = Math.max(D[i][j], prevScore + bScore);\n        }\n      }\n      // Update prevScore with gap penalty\n      if (M[i][j] > SCORE_MIN)\n        prevScore = Math.max(prevScore, M[i][j] + gapScore);\n      else if (i > 0 && prevScore > SCORE_MIN)\n        prevScore += gapScore;\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Best score is max of last row\n  let best = SCORE_MIN, bestJ = 0;\n  for (let j = n - 1; j < m; j++) {\n    if (M[n-1][j] > best) { best = M[n-1][j]; bestJ = j; }\n  }\n\n  // Traceback: reconstruct match positions\n  const positions = new Array(n).fill(0);\n  let j = bestJ;\n  for (let i = n - 1; i >= 0; i--) {\n    while (j >= 0 && (q[i] !== c[j] || M[i][j] <= SCORE_MIN)) j--;\n    positions[i] = j;\n    j--;\n  }\n\n  return { score: best, positions, bonus, D, M };\n}\n\n// ── Live scorer ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction renderLive() {\n  const query     = document.getElementById('sc-query').value;\n  const candidate = document.getElementById('sc-candidate').value;\n  const visEl     = document.getElementById('live-candidate');\n  const brkEl     = document.getElementById('live-breakdown');\n\n  if (!query || !candidate) { visEl.innerHTML = ''; brkEl.innerHTML = ''; return; }\n\n  if (!isSubseq(query.toLowerCase(), candidate.toLowerCase())) {\n    visEl.innerHTML = `<span style=\"color:var(--danger)\">✗ Not a subsequence — no match.</span>`;\n    brkEl.innerHTML = '';\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const result = score(query, candidate);\n  const { positions, bonus: bonuses } = result;\n  const posSet = new Set(positions);\n\n  // Build character breakdown\n  const events = [];\n  let consecutive = 0;\n  const chars = candidate.split('').map((ch, idx) => {\n    if (!posSet.has(idx)) {\n      const isLeadingOrTrailing =\n        idx < positions[0] || idx > positions[positions.length - 1];\n      return `<span class=\"ch ${isLeadingOrTrailing ? 'gap-outer' : 'gap-inner'}\">${ch}</span>`;\n    }\n    const queryIdx = positions.indexOf(idx);\n    const b = bonuses[idx];\n    const prevPos = queryIdx > 0 ? positions[queryIdx - 1] : -1;\n    const isConsec = prevPos === idx - 1;\n    let cls = 'm-plain';\n    let type = 'match';\n    if (isConsec && b > 0)       { cls = 'm-consec'; type = 'consecutive + boundary'; }\n    else if (isConsec)           { cls = 'm-consec'; type = 'consecutive'; }\n    else if (b >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD) { cls = 'm-boundary'; type = 'boundary'; }\n\n    const bonusLabel = b > 0 ? ` (+${b.toFixed(1)} boundary)` : '';\n    const consecLabel = isConsec ? ` (+1.0 consecutive)` : '';\n    events.push({ ch, type, bonus: b, isConsec, consecLabel, bonusLabel });\n    return `<span class=\"ch ${cls}\" title=\"${type}${bonusLabel}${consecLabel}\">${ch}</span>`;\n  }).join('');\n\n  visEl.innerHTML = chars;\n\n  // Score breakdown\n  let html = `<div style=\"margin-top:0.6rem;\">`;\n  html += `<div style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.82rem;color:var(--muted);margin-bottom:0.4rem;\">Score components</div>`;\n  events.forEach(ev => {\n    let parts = [];\n    if (ev.b > 0) parts.push(`<span style=\"color:var(--accent)\">+${ev.b.toFixed(2)} boundary</span>`);\n    if (ev.isConsec) parts.push(`<span style=\"color:var(--success)\">+1.00 consecutive</span>`);\n    html += `<div class=\"breakdown-row\">\n      <span><code>${ev.ch}</code> — ${ev.type}</span>\n      <span>${parts.length ? parts.join(' ') : '<span style=\"color:var(--faint)\">+0.00</span>'}</span>\n    </div>`;\n  });\n  html += `<div class=\"breakdown-row\" style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;border-top:2px solid var(--ink);\">\n    <strong>Total score</strong>\n    <strong id=\"live-total\">${result.score.toFixed(3)}</strong>\n  </div>`;\n  html += `</div>`;\n  brkEl.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\ndocument.getElementById('sc-query').addEventListener('input', renderLive);\ndocument.getElementById('sc-candidate').addEventListener('input', renderLive);\nrenderLive();\n\n// ── Ranking demo ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction renderRanking() {\n  const query = 'cfg';\n  const candidates = [\n    'cfg.ts',\n    'auth_config_loader.ts',\n    'app_configuration_manager.ts',\n    'reconfiguring_cache.json',\n  ];\n\n  const scored = candidates.map(c => ({ c, ...score(query, c) }));\n  scored.sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);\n\n  const el = document.getElementById('ranking-demo');\n  let html = '';\n  scored.forEach((item, rank) => {\n    const { positions, bonus: bonuses } = item;\n    const posSet = new Set(positions);\n    const chars = item.c.split('').map((ch, idx) => {\n      if (!posSet.has(idx)) {\n        const outer = idx < positions[0] || idx > positions[positions.length - 1];\n        return `<span class=\"ch ${outer ? 'gap-outer' : 'gap-inner'}\">${ch}</span>`;\n      }\n      const qi = positions.indexOf(idx);\n      const b = bonuses[idx];\n      const isConsec = qi > 0 && positions[qi-1] === idx - 1;\n      let cls = isConsec ? 'm-consec' : b >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD ? 'm-boundary' : 'm-plain';\n      return `<span class=\"ch ${cls}\">${ch}</span>`;\n    }).join('');\n\n    html += `<div style=\"border:1px solid var(--rule);border-radius:6px;padding:0.75rem 1rem;margin-bottom:0.6rem;background:${rank===0?'var(--success-bg)':'#fafafa'}\">\n      <div style=\"display:flex;justify-content:space-between;align-items:baseline;margin-bottom:0.3rem;\">\n        <span style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;font-weight:700;color:${rank===0?'var(--success)':'var(--muted)'};\">#${rank+1}</span>\n        <span style=\"font-family:var(--mono);font-size:0.82rem;color:var(--muted);\">score: ${item.score.toFixed(3)}</span>\n      </div>\n      <div class=\"candidate-line\" style=\"font-size:0.95rem;\">${chars}</div>\n    </div>`;\n  });\n  el.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nrenderRanking();\n\n// ── Quiz ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}

Opening in existing browser session.

Lesson 5 is open — the most substantial one in the course.

**What it covers:**

Three scoring decisions, each solving a specific failure of naive subsequence matching:

1. **Consecutive bonus (+1.0 per pair)** — `cfg` matching three consecutive chars in `cfg.ts` is more intentional than the same three chars scattered across `configuration`. The demo shows this directly.

2. **Word boundary bonus (+0.6 to +0.9)** — matching after `/`, `_`, `.`, or a camelCase capital means you're thinking about word structure, not just character presence. The table shows all boundary types and their weights.

3. **Affine gap penalty** — borrowed from bioinformatics. One long gap is more forgivable than many short gaps, so opening a gap costs more than extending one.

**The live scorer** is the centrepiece: type any query and candidate, and it renders each matched character colour-coded (green = consecutive, blue = boundary, yellow = plain match, red underline = inner gap) with a point-by-point breakdown and total score.

**The ranking demo** shows four candidates for query `cfg` already sorted by score so you can see the model's output immediately.

After the quizzes, there's one more lesson: Lesson 6 on the Bitap algorithm — why the scoring DP is O(mn) and how bit-parallel operations can compute approximate matches much faster for short queries.

color: #166534; font-weight: 800; }\n    .ch.m-boundary { background: #dbeafe; color: #1e40af; font-weight: 800; }\n    .ch.m-plain    { background: #fef9c3; color: #92400e; font-weight: 700; }\n    .ch.gap-inner  { color: #dc2626; text-decoration: underline; text-decoration-style: dotted; }\n    .ch.gap-outer  { color: var(--faint); }\n\n    .comparison-grid {\n      display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr;\n      gap: 0.75rem; margin: 1rem 0;\n    }\n    @media (max-width: 580px) { .comparison-grid { grid-template-columns: 1fr; } }\n\n    .comp-card {\n      border: 1px solid var(--rule); border-radius: 6px;\n      padding: 0.85rem 1rem; background: #fafafa;\n    }\n    .comp-card.winner { border-color: var(--success); background: var(--success-bg); }\n    .comp-card .label {\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.75rem; font-weight: 700;\n      text-transform: uppercase; letter-spacing: 0.07em;\n      color: var(--muted); margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\n    }\n    .comp-card.winner .label { color: var(--success); }\n    .comp-score { font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 1.1rem; font-weight: 700; }\n\n    .bonus-table { width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 0.88rem; margin: 1rem 0; }\n    .bonus-table th { text-align: left; font-family: var(--sans); font-weight: 600;\n      padding: 0.4rem 0.6rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--rule); }\n    .bonus-table td { padding: 0.35rem 0.6rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--rule); font-family: var(--mono); }\n    .bonus-table td:last-child { font-weight: 700; }\n\n    .score-legend { display: flex; gap: 0.9rem; flex-wrap: wrap;\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.8rem; margin: 0.5rem 0 1rem; }\n    .score-legend span { display: flex; align-items: center; gap: 0.35rem; }\n    .score-legend .sw { width: 0.9rem; height: 0.9rem; border-radius: 2px; border: 1px solid var(--rule); flex-shrink: 0; }\n\n    /* ── Live scorer ── */\n    #live-candidate { font-size: 1.15rem; word-break: break-all; min-height: 2rem; margin: 0.5rem 0; line-height: 1.9; }\n    #live-breakdown { font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.88rem; margin-top: 0.5rem; }\n    #live-total { font-size: 1.2rem; font-weight: 700; font-family: var(--mono); color: var(--accent); }\n    .breakdown-row { display: flex; justify-content: space-between;\n      border-bottom: 1px solid var(--rule); padding: 0.22rem 0; font-size: 0.85rem; }\n    .breakdown-row:last-child { border-bottom: none; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5 of 6</div>\n  <h1>The Scoring Model</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: rank matches by intent, not just by existence</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  After the subsequence gate (Lesson 4), we know a query's characters all\n  appear in the candidate in order. But a query like <code>cfg</code> matches\n  <code>cfg.ts</code> and <code>app_configuration_manager.ts</code> equally\n  — both are valid subsequences. How do we know which one the user meant?\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  Assign each match a <strong>score</strong> based on the quality of the\n  alignment, not just its existence. The scoring model encodes human\n  intuitions about intentionality: <em>consecutive runs are more deliberate\n  than scattered letters; matching word starts shows structural awareness;\n  compact matches in short strings are more precise.</em>\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  This is the heart of fzy's algorithm. Every design decision in the scoring\n  model solves one specific failure of naive subsequence matching.\n</p>\n\n<h2>The three scoring decisions</h2>\n\n<h3>Decision 1 — Consecutive match bonus</h3>\n\n<p>\n  If matched characters run consecutively in the candidate, the user almost\n  certainly typed exactly that substring. Award a large bonus per consecutive\n  pair.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"comparison-grid\">\n  <div class=\"comp-card\">\n    <div class=\"label\">Scattered match</div>\n    <div class=\"candidate-line\">\n      <span class=\"ch m-plain\">c</span>on<span class=\"ch gap-inner\">f</span>i<span class=\"ch gap-inner\">g</span>uration\n    </div>\n    <div>query <code>cfg</code> matched to positions 0, 3, 5 — gaps between every char</div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"comp-card winner\">\n    <div class=\"label\">Consecutive match ✓ wins</div>\n    <div class=\"candidate-line\">\n      <span class=\"ch m-boundary\">c</span><span class=\"ch m-consec\">f</span><span class=\"ch m-consec\">g</span>.ts\n    </div>\n    <div>query <code>cfg</code> matched to positions 0, 1, 2 — three consecutive characters</div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h3>Decision 2 — Word boundary bonus</h3>\n\n<p>\n  Matching the first character of a word (after <code>/</code>, <code>_</code>,\n  <code>-</code>, space, <code>.</code>, or uppercase-after-lowercase) means\n  the user is thinking in terms of structure, not raw characters.\n  Award a bonus scaled by boundary type.\n</p>\n\n<table class=\"bonus-table\">\n  <thead><tr><th>Boundary type</th><th>Example trigger</th><th>Bonus</th></tr></thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td>Path separator <code>/</code></td><td><code>/usr/<strong>l</strong>ocal</code></td><td>+0.9</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Word char <code>_ - space</code></td><td><code>auth_<strong>c</strong>onfig</code></td><td>+0.8</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>camelCase capital</td><td><code>my<strong>C</strong>omponent</code></td><td>+0.8</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Dot separator</td><td><code>index.<strong>t</strong>s</code></td><td>+0.6</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>No boundary</td><td><code>con<strong>f</strong>ig</code></td><td>+0.0</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why these values?</span>\n  Path separators rank highest because typing <code>usr/l</code> precisely signals\n  you want something <em>inside</em> <code>/usr/</code>. Word chars are next —\n  they show you know the token structure. Mid-word matches are penalised\n  because they could easily be accidental.\n</div>\n\n<h3>Decision 3 — Gap penalty (affine)</h3>\n\n<p>\n  Every unmatched character between two matched characters is a \"gap.\"\n  Gaps are penalised because they suggest the match was accidental.\n  fzy uses an <strong>affine gap penalty</strong>: a fixed cost for\n  <em>opening</em> a gap, plus a smaller cost per additional character in it.\n</p>\n\n<pre>gap_cost(length) = GAP_OPEN + (length - 1) × GAP_EXTEND\n\nwhere: GAP_OPEN = -0.01   (per character, inner gaps)\n       Outer gaps (leading/trailing) = -0.005 per character</pre>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why affine and not linear?</span>\n  Borrowed from bioinformatics (Gotoh, 1982). A single long gap is more\n  \"forgivable\" than many short gaps: one long skip might just mean the\n  file has a long suffix. Many small gaps suggest the match is scattered\n  by coincidence. Affine penalties encode this by making the first character\n  of a gap more expensive than subsequent ones.\n</div>\n\n<h2>The two-matrix DP</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The scoring DP builds two matrices over the same (query × candidate) grid:\n</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <strong>M[i][j]</strong> — the best score for matching the first <code>i</code>\n    query characters to the first <code>j</code> candidate characters,\n    with query[i] matched to candidate[j]. May have arrived here via a gap.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <strong>D[i][j]</strong> — the same, but <em>query[i] is part of a\n    consecutive run</em> (no gap before this match). Used to compute the\n    consecutive bonus correctly.\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<pre>// Bonus at candidate position j\nB[j] = boundary_bonus(candidate, j)\n\n// D: consecutive-run score ending at (i, j)\nD[i][j] = max(\n  M[i-1][j-1] + CONSECUTIVE + B[j],   // extend a run from any previous match\n  D[i-1][j-1] + CONSECUTIVE + B[j]    // extend a confirmed consecutive run\n)\n\n// M: best score overall ending at (i, j)\nM[i][j] = max(\n  D[i][j],                             // end a consecutive run here\n  best over k < j: M[i-1][k] + gap_cost(j - k) + B[j]\n)</pre>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Why two matrices?</span>\n  The consecutive bonus applies when <em>both</em> the previous and current\n  query characters are matched without a gap. If you tracked only one matrix\n  you couldn't distinguish \"I arrived here from a consecutive run\" from\n  \"I arrived here via a gap.\" The D matrix carries that information.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Live scorer</h2>\n\n<p>Type a query and candidate to see the fzy-style score and alignment.</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\">\n  <h3>Scoring explorer</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:120px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Query</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sc-query\" value=\"cfg\" maxlength=\"12\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:2;min-width:200px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Candidate</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sc-candidate\" value=\"auth_config_loader.ts\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"score-legend\">\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#dcfce7;border-color:#16a34a;\"></span> Consecutive match</span>\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#dbeafe;border-color:#3b82f6;\"></span> Boundary match</span>\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#fef9c3;border-color:#ca8a04;\"></span> Plain match</span>\n    <span><span class=\"sw\" style=\"background:#fee2e2;border-color:#dc2626;\"></span> Inner gap</span>\n  </div>\n  <div id=\"live-candidate\" class=\"candidate-line\"></div>\n  <div id=\"live-breakdown\"></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Seeing the ranking in action</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Below are four candidates for query <code>cfg</code>, ranked by their\n  fzy score. Hover over each to see why it ranks where it does.\n</p>\n\n<div id=\"ranking-demo\"></div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. Query <code>mc</code> against <code>MyComponent.tsx</code>. The M matches at position 0 (capital, start of string) and the C at position 2 (camelCase capital). What type of bonus applies to both?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> Consecutive match bonus — the characters run one after another</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Boundary bonus — both M and C are at camelCase word boundaries</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Gap penalty — there is one character between M and C</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> Path separator bonus — the file extension creates a boundary</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. M is at position 0 (start of string = highest boundary bonus), C is a capital after lowercase (camelCase boundary). Both earn +0.8 or higher.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. Why does fzy use an <em>affine</em> gap penalty rather than a flat penalty per gap character?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> To make the score always a negative number</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> One long gap is more forgivable than many short gaps — affine makes opening a gap cost more than extending it</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> To ensure the score is comparable across strings of different lengths</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> Affine penalties are faster to compute than linear ones</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. Many short gaps suggest scattered/accidental matching. One long gap might just be a long file suffix. Affine penalty encodes this: pay more to open a gap, less to extend an existing one.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. The scoring DP uses two matrices: M and D. What specifically does the D matrix track that M alone cannot?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> Whether the current match character is uppercase</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> The best score where the current match is part of a consecutive run (no gap before it)</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> The cumulative gap penalty across the entire candidate</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> The minimum number of gaps needed to complete the match</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. D[i][j] tracks the score when query[i] arrived at candidate[j] without a gap from the previous match. This is needed to correctly apply the consecutive bonus, which only fires when both the current and previous matches were adjacent.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. Query <code>ts</code>. Candidate A: <code>tools.ts</code> (matches <code>t</code> at position 0, <code>s</code> at position 7 after the dot). Candidate B: <code>timestamp.js</code> (matches <code>t</code> at 0, <code>s</code> at 4 consecutively as part of \"times\"). Which scores higher and why?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> A scores higher — the dot before .ts is a boundary, giving a large bonus to s</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> B scores higher — ts appears consecutively near the start with no gap bonus needed</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> They score equally — both match t at position 0</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> A scores higher — shorter strings always rank above longer ones</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','a','Correct. In tools.ts the s matches after a dot boundary (+0.6) and t matches at position 0. This is the intended match — the user typed ts to find TypeScript files. The dot-boundary bonus on s elevates it above a mid-word consecutive match with no boundary signal.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://github.com/jhawthorn/fzy/blob/master/ALGORITHM.md\" target=\"_blank\">\n    fzy ALGORITHM.md — jhawthorn (GitHub)\n  </a>\n  — You now have everything you need to read this document end-to-end and\n  understand every paragraph. Read it now: the gap score, the bonus values,\n  the two-matrix DP, and the rationale for each constant.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat and I'll go deeper on any scoring decision, matrix cell, or constant from this lesson.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0004-threshold-search.html\">← Lesson 4: From Distance to Search</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5 of 6</span>\n  <a href=\"0006-bitap.html\">Next: The Bitap Algorithm →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── Scoring constants (fzy-faithful) ─────────────────────────────────────────\nconst SCORE_GAP_LEADING    = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_TRAILING   = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_INNER      = -0.01;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE = 1.0;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_SLASH    = 0.9;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_WORD     = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL  = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_DOT      = 0.6;\nconst SCORE_MIN            = -Infinity;\n\nfunction charBonus(str, i) {\n  if (i === 0) return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  const prev = str[i - 1], cur = str[i];\n  if (prev === '/' || prev === '\\\\') return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  if (prev === '_' || prev === '-' || prev === ' ') return SCORE_MATCH_WORD;\n  if (prev === '.') return SCORE_MATCH_DOT;\n  if (cur >= 'A' && cur <= 'Z' && prev >= 'a' && prev <= 'z') return SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL;\n  return 0;\n}\n\nfunction isSubseq(query, candidate) {\n  const q = query.toLowerCase(), c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  let qi = 0;\n  for (let ci = 0; ci < c.length && qi < q.length; ci++)\n    if (c[ci] === q[qi]) qi++;\n  return qi === q.length;\n}\n\nfunction score(query, candidate) {\n  const n = query.length, m = candidate.length;\n  const q = query.toLowerCase(), c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  if (!isSubseq(q, c)) return { score: SCORE_MIN, positions: [] };\n\n  // Precompute bonuses\n  const bonus = Array.from({length: m}, (_, i) => charBonus(candidate, i));\n\n  // Two matrices: D (consecutive), M (best overall)\n  // Initialise with -Infinity\n  const D = Array.from({length: n}, () => new Float64Array(m).fill(SCORE_MIN));\n  const M = Array.from({length: n}, () => new Float64Array(m).fill(SCORE_MIN));\n\n  for (let i = 0; i < n; i++) {\n    let prevScore = SCORE_MIN;\n    const gapScore = i === n - 1 ? SCORE_GAP_TRAILING : SCORE_GAP_INNER;\n\n    for (let j = (i === 0 ? 0 : i); j < m; j++) {\n      if (q[i] === c[j]) {\n        let bScore = bonus[j];\n        if (i === 0) {\n          // First query char: leading gap from start\n          const leadGap = j * SCORE_GAP_LEADING;\n          D[i][j] = leadGap + bScore;\n          M[i][j] = D[i][j];\n        } else {\n          // D: consecutive from previous query char at j-1\n          const dVal = j > 0 && D[i-1][j-1] > SCORE_MIN\n            ? D[i-1][j-1] + SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE + bScore\n            : SCORE_MIN;\n          // Also: M from j-1 + consecutive (extending any match)\n          const mVal = j > 0 && M[i-1][j-1] > SCORE_MIN\n            ? M[i-1][j-1] + SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE + bScore\n            : SCORE_MIN;\n          D[i][j] = Math.max(dVal, mVal);\n          M[i][j] = Math.max(D[i][j], prevScore + bScore);\n        }\n      }\n      // Update prevScore with gap penalty\n      if (M[i][j] > SCORE_MIN)\n        prevScore = Math.max(prevScore, M[i][j] + gapScore);\n      else if (i > 0 && prevScore > SCORE_MIN)\n        prevScore += gapScore;\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Best score is max of last row\n  let best = SCORE_MIN, bestJ = 0;\n  for (let j = n - 1; j < m; j++) {\n    if (M[n-1][j] > best) { best = M[n-1][j]; bestJ = j; }\n  }\n\n  // Traceback: reconstruct match positions\n  const positions = new Array(n).fill(0);\n  let j = bestJ;\n  for (let i = n - 1; i >= 0; i--) {\n    while (j >= 0 && (q[i] !== c[j] || M[i][j] <= SCORE_MIN)) j--;\n    positions[i] = j;\n    j--;\n  }\n\n  return { score: best, positions, bonus, D, M };\n}\n\n// ── Live scorer ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction renderLive() {\n  const query     = document.getElementById('sc-query').value;\n  const candidate = document.getElementById('sc-candidate').value;\n  const visEl     = document.getElementById('live-candidate');\n  const brkEl     = document.getElementById('live-breakdown');\n\n  if (!query || !candidate) { visEl.innerHTML = ''; brkEl.innerHTML = ''; return; }\n\n  if (!isSubseq(query.toLowerCase(), candidate.toLowerCase())) {\n    visEl.innerHTML = `<span style=\"color:var(--danger)\">✗ Not a subsequence — no match.</span>`;\n    brkEl.innerHTML = '';\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const result = score(query, candidate);\n  const { positions, bonus: bonuses } = result;\n  const posSet = new Set(positions);\n\n  // Build character breakdown\n  const events = [];\n  let consecutive = 0;\n  const chars = candidate.split('').map((ch, idx) => {\n    if (!posSet.has(idx)) {\n      const isLeadingOrTrailing =\n        idx < positions[0] || idx > positions[positions.length - 1];\n      return `<span class=\"ch ${isLeadingOrTrailing ? 'gap-outer' : 'gap-inner'}\">${ch}</span>`;\n    }\n    const queryIdx = positions.indexOf(idx);\n    const b = bonuses[idx];\n    const prevPos = queryIdx > 0 ? positions[queryIdx - 1] : -1;\n    const isConsec = prevPos === idx - 1;\n    let cls = 'm-plain';\n    let type = 'match';\n    if (isConsec && b > 0)       { cls = 'm-consec'; type = 'consecutive + boundary'; }\n    else if (isConsec)           { cls = 'm-consec'; type = 'consecutive'; }\n    else if (b >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD) { cls = 'm-boundary'; type = 'boundary'; }\n\n    const bonusLabel = b > 0 ? ` (+${b.toFixed(1)} boundary)` : '';\n    const consecLabel = isConsec ? ` (+1.0 consecutive)` : '';\n    events.push({ ch, type, bonus: b, isConsec, consecLabel, bonusLabel });\n    return `<span class=\"ch ${cls}\" title=\"${type}${bonusLabel}${consecLabel}\">${ch}</span>`;\n  }).join('');\n\n  visEl.innerHTML = chars;\n\n  // Score breakdown\n  let html = `<div style=\"margin-top:0.6rem;\">`;\n  html += `<div style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.82rem;color:var(--muted);margin-bottom:0.4rem;\">Score components</div>`;\n  events.forEach(ev => {\n    let parts = [];\n    if (ev.b > 0) parts.push(`<span style=\"color:var(--accent)\">+${ev.b.toFixed(2)} boundary</span>`);\n    if (ev.isConsec) parts.push(`<span style=\"color:var(--success)\">+1.00 consecutive</span>`);\n    html += `<div class=\"breakdown-row\">\n      <span><code>${ev.ch}</code> — ${ev.type}</span>\n      <span>${parts.length ? parts.join(' ') : '<span style=\"color:var(--faint)\">+0.00</span>'}</span>\n    </div>`;\n  });\n  html += `<div class=\"breakdown-row\" style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;border-top:2px solid var(--ink);\">\n    <strong>Total score</strong>\n    <strong id=\"live-total\">${result.score.toFixed(3)}</strong>\n  </div>`;\n  html += `</div>`;\n  brkEl.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\ndocument.getElementById('sc-query').addEventListener('input', renderLive);\ndocument.getElementById('sc-candidate').addEventListener('input', renderLive);\nrenderLive();\n\n// ── Ranking demo ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction renderRanking() {\n  const query = 'cfg';\n  const candidates = [\n    'cfg.ts',\n    'auth_config_loader.ts',\n    'app_configuration_manager.ts',\n    'reconfiguring_cache.json',\n  ];\n\n  const scored = candidates.map(c => ({ c, ...score(query, c) }));\n  scored.sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);\n\n  const el = document.getElementById('ranking-demo');\n  let html = '';\n  scored.forEach((item, rank) => {\n    const { positions, bonus: bonuses } = item;\n    const posSet = new Set(positions);\n    const chars = item.c.split('').map((ch, idx) => {\n      if (!posSet.has(idx)) {\n        const outer = idx < positions[0] || idx > positions[positions.length - 1];\n        return `<span class=\"ch ${outer ? 'gap-outer' : 'gap-inner'}\">${ch}</span>`;\n      }\n      const qi = positions.indexOf(idx);\n      const b = bonuses[idx];\n      const isConsec = qi > 0 && positions[qi-1] === idx - 1;\n      let cls = isConsec ? 'm-consec' : b >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD ? 'm-boundary' : 'm-plain';\n      return `<span class=\"ch ${cls}\">${ch}</span>`;\n    }).join('');\n\n    html += `<div style=\"border:1px solid var(--rule);border-radius:6px;padding:0.75rem 1rem;margin-bottom:0.6rem;background:${rank===0?'var(--success-bg)':'#fafafa'}\">\n      <div style=\"display:flex;justify-content:space-between;align-items:baseline;margin-bottom:0.3rem;\">\n        <span style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;font-weight:700;color:${rank===0?'var(--success)':'var(--muted)'};\">#${rank+1}</span>\n        <span style=\"font-family:var(--mono);font-size:0.82rem;color:var(--muted);\">score: ${item.score.toFixed(3)}</span>\n      </div>\n      <div class=\"candidate-line\" style=\"font-size:0.95rem;\">${chars}</div>\n    </div>`;\n  });\n  el.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nrenderRanking();\n\n// ── Quiz ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}

### User (Turn 15)

what does "affine" mean? is it a mathematical term?

### Assistant (Turn 16)

Yes, it's a mathematical term, though used loosely here.

In strict mathematics, an **affine function** is one of the form `f(x) = ax + b` — a linear function with a constant offset. The key property is that it's linear *after the first step*: the first unit costs something different (the offset `b`), and every subsequent unit costs the same fixed rate `a`.

That's exactly what the gap penalty does:

```
gap_cost(length) = OPEN + (length - 1) × EXTEND

gap of 1:  OPEN                        (just the fixed cost)
gap of 2:  OPEN + EXTEND
gap of 3:  OPEN + EXTEND + EXTEND
```

The *first* character of a gap is expensive (you pay `OPEN`). Each *additional* character in the same gap is cheaper (you pay `EXTEND`). That's the affine shape — a jump at step one, then a steady slope after.

The term comes from **bioinformatics**, where the same trick is used when aligning DNA sequences. Gotoh (1982) introduced affine gap penalties because a single 10-base deletion in DNA is biologically more likely than ten separate 1-base deletions — the same intuition fzy borrows for fuzzy matching.

So "affine gap penalty" just means: *opening a gap costs more than continuing one*.

write a "sublesson" exploring how the scoring algorithm behaves when there are multiple matches of query in candidate, for instance query=ts candidate=timestamp.ts

  "content": "<!DOCTYPE html>\n<html lang=\"en\">\n<head>\n  <meta charset=\"UTF-8\">\n  <meta name=\"viewport\" content=\"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0\">\n  <title>Lesson 5b — Competing Alignments</title>\n  <link rel=\"stylesheet\" href=\"../assets/style.css\">\n  <style>\n    .ch { display: inline-block; padding: 0 0.05em; border-radius: 2px; font-family: var(--mono); }\n    .ch.m-consec   { background: #dcfce7; color: #166534; font-weight: 800; }\n    .ch.m-boundary { background: #dbeafe; color: #1e40af; color: #166534; }\n    .why-bound   { background: #dbeafe; color: #1e40af; }\n    .why-gap     { background: #fee2e2; color: #dc2626; }\n    .why-start   { background: #f3e8ff; color: #7e22ce; }\n\n    #no-alignments {\n      font-family: var(--sans);\n      color: var(--danger);\n      font-size: 0.9rem;\n      margin: 0.75rem 0;\n    }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5b — Sublesson</div>\n  <h1>Competing Alignments</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">When a query can match in multiple places, how does scoring choose?</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The hidden complexity of subsequence matching</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Lesson 5 described the scoring rules in isolation. But there is a subtlety\n  we glossed over: for a given query and candidate, there may be\n  <strong>many valid subsequence alignments</strong> — many different ways to\n  assign each query character to a candidate position.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  The scoring DP does not pick one alignment upfront. It evaluates\n  <em>all of them simultaneously</em> by filling the M and D matrices,\n  and the winner emerges from the recurrence naturally.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The motivating example</span>\n  Query <code>ts</code>, candidate <code>timestamp.ts</code>.<br><br>\n  The characters <code>t</code> and <code>s</code> both appear multiple times.\n  <code>t</code> is at positions 0, 5, 10 — and <code>s</code> is at positions 4\n  and 11. That gives <strong>four valid alignments</strong>. Which one should win?\n</div>\n\n<h2>Enumerating the alignments</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Let's lay out every valid alignment for <code>ts</code> in\n  <code>timestamp.ts</code> and score each one manually before looking at\n  what the algorithm picks.\n</p>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"width:100%;margin:1rem 0;font-size:0.85rem;\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr><th>t position</th><th>s position</th><th>t bonus</th><th>s bonus</th><th>Consec?</th><th>Gap penalty</th><th>Approx score</th></tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>0 — start of string</td><td>4 — mid-word</td>\n      <td>+0.90</td><td>+0.00</td><td>✗</td>\n      <td>−0.03 (3 inner)</td><td>≈ 0.87</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>0 — start of string</td><td>11 — after dot</td>\n      <td>+0.90</td><td>+0.00</td><td>✗</td>\n      <td>−0.10 (10 inner)</td><td>≈ 0.80</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>5 — mid-word</td><td>11 — after dot</td>\n      <td>+0.00</td><td>+0.00</td><td>✗</td>\n      <td>−0.025 leading + −0.05 inner</td><td>≈ −0.08</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr style=\"background:var(--success-bg);font-weight:600;\">\n      <td>10 — after dot</td><td>11 — consecutive</td>\n      <td>+0.60</td><td>+1.00 consecutive</td><td>✓</td>\n      <td>−0.05 leading</td><td>≈ 1.55</td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<p>\n  The alignment that matches <code>.ts</code> at the end wins — by a large\n  margin. The consecutive bonus (+1.0) and dot boundary bonus (+0.6) together\n  dominate the leading gap penalty (−0.05 for 10 skipped chars).\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">This is the right answer</span>\n  A user who types <code>ts</code> in a file picker almost certainly wants\n  TypeScript files ending in <code>.ts</code>. The scoring model reaches\n  this conclusion automatically — not through hardcoded file-extension logic,\n  but through the interaction of the consecutive bonus and boundary bonus.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Why the DP finds this without enumerating explicitly</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The matrix recurrence means the DP \"tries\" all alignments at once.\n  At each cell <code>M[i][j]</code>, it considers:\n</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>Arriving <strong>consecutively</strong> from the previous match (via <code>D[i-1][j-1]</code>)</li>\n  <li>Arriving <strong>after a gap</strong> from the best earlier match (via <code>prevScore</code>)</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>\n  The cell simply keeps whichever is larger. No explicit enumeration. By the\n  time we reach the last query character, the cell with the highest value\n  represents the best alignment — whatever it turned out to be.\n</p>\n\n<h2>Explore: all alignments for any query and candidate</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The demo below enumerates every valid alignment explicitly, scores each one,\n  and sorts them. You can see exactly which alignment the algorithm would choose\n  and why it beats the alternatives.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\">\n  <h3>Alignment explorer</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:100px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Query</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"al-query\" value=\"ts\" maxlength=\"6\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:3;min-width:200px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Candidate</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"al-candidate\" value=\"timestamp.ts\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div id=\"no-alignments\" style=\"display:none;\">No subsequence match — query characters don't all appear in order.</div>\n  <div id=\"alignment-count\" style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.82rem;color:var(--muted);margin-bottom:0.5rem;\"></div>\n  <div id=\"alignment-list\"></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Interesting cases to try</h2>\n\n<p>Try these in the explorer above to build intuition:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <code>ts</code> / <code>tests.ts</code> — does the final <code>.ts</code>\n    still win, or does the <code>ts</code> in \"tests\" compete?\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <code>mc</code> / <code>MyComponent.tsx</code> — camelCase boundaries\n    vs any other <code>m</code>…<code>c</code> pairing.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <code>us</code> / <code>/usr/local/share</code> — path separator bonus\n    on the leading <code>u</code>.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <code>ss</code> / <code>assessments.ts</code> — two of the same\n    character: which consecutive pair wins?\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. For query <code>ts</code> in <code>timestamp.ts</code>, alignment (t=10, s=11) wins despite a leading gap of 10 skipped characters. What two bonuses overcome that penalty?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> Start-of-string bonus on t, and word-underscore bonus on s</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Dot-boundary bonus on t (+0.6), and consecutive match bonus on s (+1.0)</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Consecutive bonus on both t and s (+1.0 each)</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> Path-separator bonus on t (+0.9), and dot-boundary bonus on s (+0.6)</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. t at position 10 follows a dot (.ts), earning +0.6. s at position 11 follows t consecutively, earning +1.0. Together they give +1.6, far exceeding the −0.05 leading gap penalty.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. The DP reaches the winning alignment without explicitly listing all possibilities. How?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> It only ever tries the first occurrence of each query character</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> At each cell it keeps whichever arrival route (consecutive or gapped) gives the higher score — all routes are considered implicitly</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> It tries alignments right-to-left and stops at the first match</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> It pre-filters candidate positions using a hash of the query</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. The recurrence max(consecutive arrival, gapped arrival) means every valid alignment is implicitly evaluated. No explicit enumeration needed — the cell just keeps the best seen so far.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. Query <code>ss</code>, candidate <code>assessments</code>. Positions of s: 1, 3, 7, 8. Which alignment scores highest?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> s=1, s=3 — first two occurrences, smallest gap</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> s=1, s=7 — matching across a longer span, penalised more</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> s=7, s=8 — consecutive pair, earning the +1.0 consecutive bonus</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> s=3, s=7 — both mid-word but closest to the centre</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','c','Correct. s=7 and s=8 are consecutive, earning +1.0. s=1 and s=3 have no consecutive bonus and a 1-character gap. The consecutive bonus reliably beats the small gap between positions 7 and 8 versus the slightly smaller leading gap to positions 1 and 3.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0005-scoring-model.html\">← Lesson 5: The Scoring Model</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5b</span>\n  <a href=\"0006-bitap.html\">Next: The Bitap Algorithm →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── Scoring constants ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nconst SCORE_GAP_LEADING    = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_TRAILING   = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_INNER      = -0.01;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE = 1.0;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_SLASH    = 0.9;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_WORD     = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL  = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_DOT      = 0.6;\n\nfunction charBonus(str, i) {\n  if (i === 0) return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  const prev = str[i-1], cur = str[i];\n  if (prev === '/' || prev === '\\\\') return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  if (prev === '_' || prev === '-' || prev === ' ') return SCORE_MATCH_WORD;\n  if (prev === '.') return SCORE_MATCH_DOT;\n  if (cur >= 'A' && cur <= 'Z' && prev >= 'a' && prev <= 'z') return SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL;\n  return 0;\n}\n\n// ── Score a fixed alignment (array of candidate positions) ────────────────────\nfunction scoreAlignment(positions, candidate) {\n  const n = positions.length;\n  const m = candidate.length;\n  let total = 0;\n  const events = [];\n\n  positions.forEach((pos, qi) => {\n    const b = charBonus(candidate, pos);\n    const isConsec = qi > 0 && positions[qi-1] === pos - 1;\n\n    // Gap penalty\n    if (qi === 0) {\n      // Leading gap\n      total += pos * SCORE_GAP_LEADING;\n    } else {\n      const gapLen = pos - positions[qi-1] - 1;\n      if (gapLen > 0) total += gapLen * SCORE_GAP_INNER;\n    }\n\n    // Trailing gap (after last matched char)\n    if (qi === n - 1) {\n      total += (m - 1 - pos) * SCORE_GAP_TRAILING;\n    }\n\n    total += b;\n    if (isConsec) total += SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE;\n\n    events.push({ pos, ch: candidate[pos], bonus: b, isConsec });\n  });\n\n  return { total, events };\n}\n\n// ── Enumerate all valid alignments (positions is strictly increasing) ─────────\nfunction enumerate(query, candidate) {\n  const q = query.toLowerCase();\n  const c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  const results = [];\n\n  // For each query char, find candidate positions where it appears\n  const charPositions = Array.from(query).map((_, qi) => {\n    const ch = q[qi];\n    const pos = [];\n    for (let ci = 0; ci < c.length; ci++) if (c[ci] === ch) pos.push(ci);\n    return pos;\n  });\n\n  function recurse(qi, minPos, chosen) {\n    if (qi === query.length) {\n      results.push([...chosen]);\n      return;\n    }\n    for (const pos of charPositions[qi]) {\n      if (pos > minPos) {\n        chosen.push(pos);\n        recurse(qi + 1, pos, chosen);\n        chosen.pop();\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n  recurse(0, -1, []);\n  return results;\n}\n\n// ── Render a candidate with a given alignment highlighted ─────────────────────\nfunction renderAlignment(candidate, positions, events) {\n  const posSet = new Set(positions);\n  const firstMatch = positions[0];\n  const lastMatch  = positions[positions.length - 1];\n  return candidate.split('').map((ch, idx) => {\n    if (!posSet.has(idx)) {\n      const outer = idx < firstMatch || idx > lastMatch;\n      return `<span class=\"ch ${outer ? 'gap-outer' : 'gap-inner'}\">${ch}</span>`;\n    }\n    const qi = positions.indexOf(idx);\n    const ev = events[qi];\n    let cls = 'm-plain';\n    if (ev.isConsec && ev.bonus > 0) cls = 'm-consec';\n    else if (ev.isConsec)            cls = 'm-consec';\n    else if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD) cls = 'm-boundary';\n    return `<span class=\"ch ${cls}\">${ch}</span>`;\n  }).join('');\n}\n\n// ── Why-tags for the winner ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction whyTags(events, positions, candidate) {\n  const tags = [];\n  events.forEach(ev => {\n    if (ev.isConsec)                         tags.push(['consec',  '+1.0 consecutive']);\n    if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_SLASH)       tags.push(['start',   '+0.9 path/start']);\n    else if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD)   tags.push(['bound',   '+0.8 word boundary']);\n    else if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_DOT)    tags.push(['bound',   '+0.6 dot boundary']);\n  });\n  const leadGap = positions[0];\n  if (leadGap > 0) tags.push(['gap', `−${(leadGap * 0.005).toFixed(3)} leading gap`]);\n  // Deduplicate\n  const seen = new Set();\n  return tags.filter(t => { const k=t[0]+t[1]; if(seen.has(k)) return false; seen.add(k); return true; });\n}\n\n// ── Main render ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction renderAlignments() {\n  const query     = document.getElementById('al-query').value;\n  const candidate = document.getElementById('al-candidate').value;\n  const listEl    = document.getElementById('alignment-list');\n  const countEl   = document.getElementById('alignment-count');\n  const noEl      = document.getElementById('no-alignments');\n\n  if (!query || !candidate) { listEl.innerHTML = ''; countEl.textContent = ''; noEl.style.display='none'; return; }\n\n  const allAlignments = enumerate(query, candidate);\n  if (allAlignments.length === 0) {\n    noEl.style.display = 'block';\n    listEl.innerHTML = '';\n    countEl.textContent = '';\n    return;\n  }\n  noEl.style.display = 'none';\n\n  // Score each alignment\n  const scored = allAlignments.map(positions => {\n    const { total, events } = scoreAlignment(positions, candidate);\n    return { positions, total, events };\n  });\n  scored.sort((a, b) => b.total - a.total);\n\n  const shown = scored.slice(0, 10);\n  const hidden = scored.length - shown.length;\n\n  countEl.textContent = `${scored.length} valid alignment${scored.length===1?'':'s'} found${hidden>0?' (showing top 10)':''}.`;\n\n  let html = '';\n  shown.forEach((item, rank) => {\n    const isWinner = rank === 0;\n    const rendered = renderAlignment(candidate, item.positions, item.events);\n    const posLabel = item.positions.map((p,i) => `${query[i]}@${p}`).join(', ');\n\n    let tagsHtml = '';\n    if (isWinner) {\n      const tags = whyTags(item.events, item.positions, candidate);\n      tagsHtml = tags.map(([type, label]) =>\n        `<span class=\"why-tag why-${type==='start'||type==='bound'?'bound':type}\">${label}</span>`\n      ).join('');\n    }\n\n    html += `<div class=\"alignment-card ${isWinner ? 'winner' : ''}\">\n      <div class=\"rank\">${isWinner ? '★ #1' : `#${rank+1}`}</div>\n      <div class=\"cand-render\">${rendered}<br>\n        <span style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.72rem;color:var(--muted);\">${posLabel}</span>\n        ${tagsHtml}\n      </div>\n      <div class=\"score-col\">${item.total.toFixed(3)}</div>\n    </div>`;\n  });\n\n  listEl.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\ndocument.getElementById('al-query').addEventListener('input', renderAlignments);\ndocument.getElementById('al-candidate').addEventListener('input', renderAlignments);\nrenderAlignments();\n\n// ── Quiz ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}

Sublesson 5b is open. Here's what the alignment explorer shows for `ts` / `timestamp.ts`:

```
★ #1  timestamp.ts   +1.55    ← t@10 (dot boundary +0.6) + s@11 (consecutive +1.0)
  #2  timestamp.ts   +0.87    ← t@0  (start +0.9) + s@4  (no bonus)
  #3  timestamp.ts   +0.80    ← t@0  (start +0.9) + s@11 (no bonus, big gap)
  #4  timestamp.ts   −0.08    ← t@5  (no bonus)  + s@11
```

The explorer enumerates **every valid alignment** explicitly, scores each one, and ranks them — so you can see directly what the DP is choosing between and why. Try the suggested cases at the bottom of the lesson:

- `ss` / `assessments` — positions 7 and 8 beat any other pair because of consecutive bonus
- `mc` / `MyComponent.tsx` — the camelCase pair beats any other m…c combination
- `us` / `/usr/local/share` — path separator bonus on `u` is enormous

The key insight the sublesson formalises: the scoring model doesn't need to "know" what a TypeScript file is. The consecutive + boundary bonus automatically surfaces `timestamp.ts` → `.ts` as the intended match. The heuristics encode intent without any domain knowledge.
