color: #166534; }\n    .why-bound   { background: #dbeafe; color: #1e40af; }\n    .why-gap     { background: #fee2e2; color: #dc2626; }\n    .why-start   { background: #f3e8ff; color: #7e22ce; }\n\n    #no-alignments {\n      font-family: var(--sans);\n      color: var(--danger);\n      font-size: 0.9rem;\n      margin: 0.75rem 0;\n    }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5b — Sublesson</div>\n  <h1>Competing Alignments</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">When a query can match in multiple places, how does scoring choose?</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The hidden complexity of subsequence matching</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Lesson 5 described the scoring rules in isolation. But there is a subtlety\n  we glossed over: for a given query and candidate, there may be\n  <strong>many valid subsequence alignments</strong> — many different ways to\n  assign each query character to a candidate position.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  The scoring DP does not pick one alignment upfront. It evaluates\n  <em>all of them simultaneously</em> by filling the M and D matrices,\n  and the winner emerges from the recurrence naturally.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The motivating example</span>\n  Query <code>ts</code>, candidate <code>timestamp.ts</code>.<br><br>\n  The characters <code>t</code> and <code>s</code> both appear multiple times.\n  <code>t</code> is at positions 0, 5, 10 — and <code>s</code> is at positions 4\n  and 11. That gives <strong>four valid alignments</strong>. Which one should win?\n</div>\n\n<h2>Enumerating the alignments</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Let's lay out every valid alignment for <code>ts</code> in\n  <code>timestamp.ts</code> and score each one manually before looking at\n  what the algorithm picks.\n</p>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"width:100%;margin:1rem 0;font-size:0.85rem;\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr><th>t position</th><th>s position</th><th>t bonus</th><th>s bonus</th><th>Consec?</th><th>Gap penalty</th><th>Approx score</th></tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>0 — start of string</td><td>4 — mid-word</td>\n      <td>+0.90</td><td>+0.00</td><td>✗</td>\n      <td>−0.03 (3 inner)</td><td>≈ 0.87</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>0 — start of string</td><td>11 — after dot</td>\n      <td>+0.90</td><td>+0.00</td><td>✗</td>\n      <td>−0.10 (10 inner)</td><td>≈ 0.80</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>5 — mid-word</td><td>11 — after dot</td>\n      <td>+0.00</td><td>+0.00</td><td>✗</td>\n      <td>−0.025 leading + −0.05 inner</td><td>≈ −0.08</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr style=\"background:var(--success-bg);font-weight:600;\">\n      <td>10 — after dot</td><td>11 — consecutive</td>\n      <td>+0.60</td><td>+1.00 consecutive</td><td>✓</td>\n      <td>−0.05 leading</td><td>≈ 1.55</td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<p>\n  The alignment that matches <code>.ts</code> at the end wins — by a large\n  margin. The consecutive bonus (+1.0) and dot boundary bonus (+0.6) together\n  dominate the leading gap penalty (−0.05 for 10 skipped chars).\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">This is the right answer</span>\n  A user who types <code>ts</code> in a file picker almost certainly wants\n  TypeScript files ending in <code>.ts</code>. The scoring model reaches\n  this conclusion automatically — not through hardcoded file-extension logic,\n  but through the interaction of the consecutive bonus and boundary bonus.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Why the DP finds this without enumerating explicitly</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The matrix recurrence means the DP \"tries\" all alignments at once.\n  At each cell <code>M[i][j]</code>, it considers:\n</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>Arriving <strong>consecutively</strong> from the previous match (via <code>D[i-1][j-1]</code>)</li>\n  <li>Arriving <strong>after a gap</strong> from the best earlier match (via <code>prevScore</code>)</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>\n  The cell simply keeps whichever is larger. No explicit enumeration. By the\n  time we reach the last query character, the cell with the highest value\n  represents the best alignment — whatever it turned out to be.\n</p>\n\n<h2>Explore: all alignments for any query and candidate</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The demo below enumerates every valid alignment explicitly, scores each one,\n  and sorts them. You can see exactly which alignment the algorithm would choose\n  and why it beats the alternatives.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\">\n  <h3>Alignment explorer</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:100px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Query</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"al-query\" value=\"ts\" maxlength=\"6\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:3;min-width:200px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Candidate</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"al-candidate\" value=\"timestamp.ts\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div id=\"no-alignments\" style=\"display:none;\">No subsequence match — query characters don't all appear in order.</div>\n  <div id=\"alignment-count\" style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.82rem;color:var(--muted);margin-bottom:0.5rem;\"></div>\n  <div id=\"alignment-list\"></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Interesting cases to try</h2>\n\n<p>Try these in the explorer above to build intuition:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <code>ts</code> / <code>tests.ts</code> — does the final <code>.ts</code>\n    still win, or does the <code>ts</code> in \"tests\" compete?\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <code>mc</code> / <code>MyComponent.tsx</code> — camelCase boundaries\n    vs any other <code>m</code>…<code>c</code> pairing.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <code>us</code> / <code>/usr/local/share</code> — path separator bonus\n    on the leading <code>u</code>.\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <code>ss</code> / <code>assessments.ts</code> — two of the same\n    character: which consecutive pair wins?\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. For query <code>ts</code> in <code>timestamp.ts</code>, alignment (t=10, s=11) wins despite a leading gap of 10 skipped characters. What two bonuses overcome that penalty?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> Start-of-string bonus on t, and word-underscore bonus on s</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> Dot-boundary bonus on t (+0.6), and consecutive match bonus on s (+1.0)</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> Consecutive bonus on both t and s (+1.0 each)</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> Path-separator bonus on t (+0.9), and dot-boundary bonus on s (+0.6)</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. t at position 10 follows a dot (.ts), earning +0.6. s at position 11 follows t consecutively, earning +1.0. Together they give +1.6, far exceeding the −0.05 leading gap penalty.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. The DP reaches the winning alignment without explicitly listing all possibilities. How?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> It only ever tries the first occurrence of each query character</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> At each cell it keeps whichever arrival route (consecutive or gapped) gives the higher score — all routes are considered implicitly</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> It tries alignments right-to-left and stops at the first match</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> It pre-filters candidate positions using a hash of the query</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. The recurrence max(consecutive arrival, gapped arrival) means every valid alignment is implicitly evaluated. No explicit enumeration needed — the cell just keeps the best seen so far.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. Query <code>ss</code>, candidate <code>assessments</code>. Positions of s: 1, 3, 7, 8. Which alignment scores highest?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> s=1, s=3 — first two occurrences, smallest gap</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> s=1, s=7 — matching across a longer span, penalised more</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> s=7, s=8 — consecutive pair, earning the +1.0 consecutive bonus</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> s=3, s=7 — both mid-word but closest to the centre</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','c','Correct. s=7 and s=8 are consecutive, earning +1.0. s=1 and s=3 have no consecutive bonus and a 1-character gap. The consecutive bonus reliably beats the small gap between positions 7 and 8 versus the slightly smaller leading gap to positions 1 and 3.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0005-scoring-model.html\">← Lesson 5: The Scoring Model</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 5b</span>\n  <a href=\"0006-bitap.html\">Next: The Bitap Algorithm →</a>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── Scoring constants ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nconst SCORE_GAP_LEADING    = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_TRAILING   = -0.005;\nconst SCORE_GAP_INNER      = -0.01;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE = 1.0;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_SLASH    = 0.9;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_WORD     = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL  = 0.8;\nconst SCORE_MATCH_DOT      = 0.6;\n\nfunction charBonus(str, i) {\n  if (i === 0) return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  const prev = str[i-1], cur = str[i];\n  if (prev === '/' || prev === '\\\\') return SCORE_MATCH_SLASH;\n  if (prev === '_' || prev === '-' || prev === ' ') return SCORE_MATCH_WORD;\n  if (prev === '.') return SCORE_MATCH_DOT;\n  if (cur >= 'A' && cur <= 'Z' && prev >= 'a' && prev <= 'z') return SCORE_MATCH_CAPITAL;\n  return 0;\n}\n\n// ── Score a fixed alignment (array of candidate positions) ────────────────────\nfunction scoreAlignment(positions, candidate) {\n  const n = positions.length;\n  const m = candidate.length;\n  let total = 0;\n  const events = [];\n\n  positions.forEach((pos, qi) => {\n    const b = charBonus(candidate, pos);\n    const isConsec = qi > 0 && positions[qi-1] === pos - 1;\n\n    // Gap penalty\n    if (qi === 0) {\n      // Leading gap\n      total += pos * SCORE_GAP_LEADING;\n    } else {\n      const gapLen = pos - positions[qi-1] - 1;\n      if (gapLen > 0) total += gapLen * SCORE_GAP_INNER;\n    }\n\n    // Trailing gap (after last matched char)\n    if (qi === n - 1) {\n      total += (m - 1 - pos) * SCORE_GAP_TRAILING;\n    }\n\n    total += b;\n    if (isConsec) total += SCORE_MATCH_CONSECUTIVE;\n\n    events.push({ pos, ch: candidate[pos], bonus: b, isConsec });\n  });\n\n  return { total, events };\n}\n\n// ── Enumerate all valid alignments (positions is strictly increasing) ─────────\nfunction enumerate(query, candidate) {\n  const q = query.toLowerCase();\n  const c = candidate.toLowerCase();\n  const results = [];\n\n  // For each query char, find candidate positions where it appears\n  const charPositions = Array.from(query).map((_, qi) => {\n    const ch = q[qi];\n    const pos = [];\n    for (let ci = 0; ci < c.length; ci++) if (c[ci] === ch) pos.push(ci);\n    return pos;\n  });\n\n  function recurse(qi, minPos, chosen) {\n    if (qi === query.length) {\n      results.push([...chosen]);\n      return;\n    }\n    for (const pos of charPositions[qi]) {\n      if (pos > minPos) {\n        chosen.push(pos);\n        recurse(qi + 1, pos, chosen);\n        chosen.pop();\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n  recurse(0, -1, []);\n  return results;\n}\n\n// ── Render a candidate with a given alignment highlighted ─────────────────────\nfunction renderAlignment(candidate, positions, events) {\n  const posSet = new Set(positions);\n  const firstMatch = positions[0];\n  const lastMatch  = positions[positions.length - 1];\n  return candidate.split('').map((ch, idx) => {\n    if (!posSet.has(idx)) {\n      const outer = idx < firstMatch || idx > lastMatch;\n      return `<span class=\"ch ${outer ? 'gap-outer' : 'gap-inner'}\">${ch}</span>`;\n    }\n    const qi = positions.indexOf(idx);\n    const ev = events[qi];\n    let cls = 'm-plain';\n    if (ev.isConsec && ev.bonus > 0) cls = 'm-consec';\n    else if (ev.isConsec)            cls = 'm-consec';\n    else if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD) cls = 'm-boundary';\n    return `<span class=\"ch ${cls}\">${ch}</span>`;\n  }).join('');\n}\n\n// ── Why-tags for the winner ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction whyTags(events, positions, candidate) {\n  const tags = [];\n  events.forEach(ev => {\n    if (ev.isConsec)                         tags.push(['consec',  '+1.0 consecutive']);\n    if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_SLASH)       tags.push(['start',   '+0.9 path/start']);\n    else if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_WORD)   tags.push(['bound',   '+0.8 word boundary']);\n    else if (ev.bonus >= SCORE_MATCH_DOT)    tags.push(['bound',   '+0.6 dot boundary']);\n  });\n  const leadGap = positions[0];\n  if (leadGap > 0) tags.push(['gap', `−${(leadGap * 0.005).toFixed(3)} leading gap`]);\n  // Deduplicate\n  const seen = new Set();\n  return tags.filter(t => { const k=t[0]+t[1]; if(seen.has(k)) return false; seen.add(k); return true; });\n}\n\n// ── Main render ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction renderAlignments() {\n  const query     = document.getElementById('al-query').value;\n  const candidate = document.getElementById('al-candidate').value;\n  const listEl    = document.getElementById('alignment-list');\n  const countEl   = document.getElementById('alignment-count');\n  const noEl      = document.getElementById('no-alignments');\n\n  if (!query || !candidate) { listEl.innerHTML = ''; countEl.textContent = ''; noEl.style.display='none'; return; }\n\n  const allAlignments = enumerate(query, candidate);\n  if (allAlignments.length === 0) {\n    noEl.style.display = 'block';\n    listEl.innerHTML = '';\n    countEl.textContent = '';\n    return;\n  }\n  noEl.style.display = 'none';\n\n  // Score each alignment\n  const scored = allAlignments.map(positions => {\n    const { total, events } = scoreAlignment(positions, candidate);\n    return { positions, total, events };\n  });\n  scored.sort((a, b) => b.total - a.total);\n\n  const shown = scored.slice(0, 10);\n  const hidden = scored.length - shown.length;\n\n  countEl.textContent = `${scored.length} valid alignment${scored.length===1?'':'s'} found${hidden>0?' (showing top 10)':''}.`;\n\n  let html = '';\n  shown.forEach((item, rank) => {\n    const isWinner = rank === 0;\n    const rendered = renderAlignment(candidate, item.positions, item.events);\n    const posLabel = item.positions.map((p,i) => `${query[i]}@${p}`).join(', ');\n\n    let tagsHtml = '';\n    if (isWinner) {\n      const tags = whyTags(item.events, item.positions, candidate);\n      tagsHtml = tags.map(([type, label]) =>\n        `<span class=\"why-tag why-${type==='start'||type==='bound'?'bound':type}\">${label}</span>`\n      ).join('');\n    }\n\n    html += `<div class=\"alignment-card ${isWinner ? 'winner' : ''}\">\n      <div class=\"rank\">${isWinner ? '★ #1' : `#${rank+1}`}</div>\n      <div class=\"cand-render\">${rendered}<br>\n        <span style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.72rem;color:var(--muted);\">${posLabel}</span>\n        ${tagsHtml}\n      </div>\n      <div class=\"score-col\">${item.total.toFixed(3)}</div>\n    </div>`;\n  });\n\n  listEl.innerHTML = html;\n}\n\ndocument.getElementById('al-query').addEventListener('input', renderAlignments);\ndocument.getElementById('al-candidate').addEventListener('input', renderAlignments);\nrenderAlignments();\n\n// ── Quiz ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}
```

border-color: #ca8a04; }\n    .text-char.past    { background: #f4f4f5; color: var(--muted); }\n    .text-char.future  { color: var(--faint); border-color: var(--rule); }\n    .text-char.found   { background: #dcfce7; border-color: var(--success); font-weight: 900; }\n\n    #step-box {\n      font-family: var(--sans); font-size: 0.88rem;\n      background: var(--accent-bg); border-radius: 6px;\n      padding: 0.8rem 1rem; margin: 0.75rem 0; min-height: 4rem;\n      line-height: 1.6;\n    }\n\n    .k-panel { margin-top: 0.5rem; }\n    .k-row { display: flex; align-items: center; gap: 0.75rem; margin: 0.25rem 0; font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 0.85rem; }\n    .k-label { min-width: 3rem; flex-shrink: 0; color: var(--muted); }\n    .k-bits { display: flex; gap: 3px; }\n\n    .nfa-diagram {\n      display: flex; align-items: center; gap: 0; margin: 1.5rem 0;\n      font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 0.9rem; overflow-x: auto;\n    }\n    .nfa-state {\n      width: 2.8rem; height: 2.8rem; border-radius: 50%;\n      border: 2px solid var(--ink); background: #fff;\n      display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: center;\n      font-weight: 700; flex-shrink: 0;\n    }\n    .nfa-state.active { background: #dbeafe; border-color: var(--accent); }\n    .nfa-state.final  { border-width: 4px; }\n    .nfa-arrow {\n      display: flex; flex-direction: column; align-items: center;\n      flex-shrink: 0; padding: 0 0.2rem;\n    }\n    .nfa-arrow .ch  { font-size: 0.75rem; color: var(--muted); margin-bottom: 0.1rem; }\n    .nfa-arrow .line { width: 2rem; height: 2px; background: var(--ink); position: relative; }\n    .nfa-arrow .line::after { content:''; position:absolute; right:-4px; top:-3px;\n      border:4px solid transparent; border-left-color:var(--ink); }\n\n    .algo-box {\n      background: var(--code-bg); border-radius: 6px; padding: 1rem 1.2rem;\n      font-family: var(--mono); font-size: 0.82rem; line-height: 1.7; margin: 1rem 0;\n    }\n    .algo-box .comment { color: var(--muted); }\n    .algo-box .kw  { color: var(--accent); }\n    .algo-box .hl  { background: #fef9c3; border-radius: 2px; padding: 0 2px; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 6 of 6</div>\n  <h1>The Bitap Algorithm</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: use bit-parallelism to make approximate matching fast</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The scoring DP from Lessons 5 and 5b runs in O(|query| × |candidate|) time\n  — polynomial, but still non-trivial when you have thousands of candidates.\n  The subsequence gate filters most of them, but a different class of\n  problems needs something faster still: <em>scanning large bodies of text</em>\n  for approximate matches, without any pre-filtering.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  Represent the matching state as a <strong>bitmask</strong>, where each bit\n  tracks whether a particular prefix of the pattern has been matched ending\n  at the current text position. A single bitwise operation advances\n  <em>all states at once</em>, exploiting the CPU's 64-bit word to do 64\n  comparisons in one instruction. This is the <strong>Bitap algorithm</strong>\n  (also called Shift-Or or Shift-And), introduced by Baeza-Yates and\n  Gonnet (1992).\n</div>\n\n<h2>The NFA intuition</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Before bitmasks, think of matching as a\n  <strong>non-deterministic finite automaton (NFA)</strong>.\n  For pattern <code>cat</code>, the NFA has one state per pattern character\n  plus a start state:\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"nfa-diagram\" id=\"nfa-cat\">\n  <!-- rendered by JS -->\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  The NFA starts in state 0. Each time a text character matches the expected\n  pattern character, the NFA moves to the next state. <em>Multiple states\n  can be active simultaneously</em> — this is the non-determinism.\n  If we ever reach the final state, we found a match.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The bitmask insight</span>\n  Instead of tracking which states are active in a set, encode them as\n  a single integer: bit <code>i</code> is 1 if state <code>i</code> is active.\n  One bitwise operation advances all active states at once.\n</div>\n\n<h2>The Shift-And algorithm (exact matching)</h2>\n\n<p>\n  <strong>Precomputation</strong>: for each character <code>c</code> in the alphabet,\n  build a mask <code>D[c]</code> where bit <code>i</code> is 1 if\n  <code>pattern[i] == c</code>.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  <strong>Scanning</strong>: maintain a state bitmask <code>R</code>\n  (initially 0). For each text character <code>t</code>:\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"algo-box\">\n<span class=\"comment\">// Shift all active states forward by one, open a new state 0, keep only</span><br>\n<span class=\"comment\">// states where the pattern character matches the current text character.</span><br>\n<br>\nR = ((R <span class=\"hl\">&lt;&lt; 1</span>) | 1) <span class=\"hl\">&amp;</span> D[t]<br>\n<br>\n<span class=\"comment\">// If bit (m-1) is set in R, the full pattern was just matched.</span><br>\n<span class=\"kw\">if</span> (R &amp; (1 &lt;&lt; (m-1))) → match found\n</div>\n\n<p>Each line decodes as:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li><code>R &lt;&lt; 1</code> — advance every active state by one position in the pattern</li>\n  <li><code>| 1</code> — always try starting a fresh match at position 0</li>\n  <li><code>&amp; D[t]</code> — discard any state where the pattern character does not match the text character</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2>Step through it</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Watch the bitmask evolve as we scan the text.\n  Bits are shown from position 0 (left) to m−1 (right).\n  A lit bit means \"a match of this many pattern chars has just been completed.\"\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\" style=\"padding:1.1rem 1.2rem;\">\n  <h3>Shift-And stepper</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:100px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Pattern</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sa-pattern\" value=\"cat\" maxlength=\"8\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:3;min-width:180px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Text</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sa-text\" value=\"concatenate\" maxlength=\"20\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"display:flex;align-items:flex-end;\">\n      <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"resetSA()\">Reset</button>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <!-- Pattern character labels -->\n  <div style=\"margin-bottom:0.3rem;\">\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\">\n      <span class=\"label\">bit #</span>\n      <div class=\"bits\" id=\"bit-indices\"></div>\n    </div>\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\">\n      <span class=\"label\">pattern</span>\n      <div class=\"bits\" id=\"pattern-chars\"></div>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div style=\"height:1px;background:var(--rule);margin:0.6rem 0;\"></div>\n\n  <!-- Text display -->\n  <div class=\"bitmask-row\" style=\"margin-bottom:0.4rem;\">\n    <span class=\"label\">text</span>\n    <div class=\"text-row\" id=\"text-chars\"></div>\n  </div>\n\n  <!-- State R -->\n  <div class=\"bitmask-row\">\n    <span class=\"label\">R</span>\n    <div class=\"bits\" id=\"r-bits\"></div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div id=\"step-box\">Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.</div>\n\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.6rem;flex-wrap:wrap;\">\n    <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" id=\"sa-next\" onclick=\"stepSA()\">Next Step</button>\n    <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"runAllSA()\">Run to end</button>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Extending to k errors (approximate matching)</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Exact matching is useful, but fuzzy search needs tolerance for errors.\n  The Bitap algorithm extends cleanly: instead of one bitmask, maintain\n  <strong>k + 1 bitmasks</strong>, one per error level.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"algo-box\">\n<span class=\"comment\">// R[j] = states reachable with exactly j errors</span><br>\n<span class=\"kw\">for</span> j = k <span class=\"kw\">downto</span> 1:<br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;R[j] = (<br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;((R[j] &lt;&lt; 1) | 1) &amp; D[t]   <span class=\"comment\">// match (same as exact)</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;| (R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1)             <span class=\"comment\">// deletion from text</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;| R[j-1]                      <span class=\"comment\">// insertion into text</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;| (R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1) &amp; ~D[t]      <span class=\"comment\">// substitution</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;)<br>\nR[0] = ((R[0] &lt;&lt; 1) | 1) &amp; D[t]   <span class=\"comment\">// exact match layer</span>\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  Each layer adds a one-step \"rescue\" from the layer below it. A state that\n  would have died (wrong character) in layer j−1 gets propagated to layer j\n  with one more error counted.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Mapping to edit operations</span>\n  <ul style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;\">\n    <li><code>R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1</code> (no AND with D[t]) — <strong>deletion</strong>: skip a text character</li>\n    <li><code>R[j-1]</code> — <strong>insertion</strong>: advance in pattern without consuming text</li>\n    <li><code>(R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1) &amp; ~D[t]</code> — <strong>substitution</strong>: consume text but allow mismatch</li>\n  </ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Try it: k-approximate matching</h2>\n\n<div class=\"demo\" style=\"padding:1.1rem 1.2rem;\">\n  <h3>Approximate match stepper (k errors)</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.75rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:80px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Pattern</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"ka-pattern\" value=\"comit\" maxlength=\"8\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:3;min-width:160px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Text</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"ka-text\" value=\"git commit\" maxlength=\"20\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:0.5;min-width:60px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">k</label>\n      <select id=\"ka-k\" style=\"width:100%;padding:0.45rem 0.3rem;border:1px solid var(--rule);border-radius:4px;\">\n        <option value=\"0\">0</option>\n        <option value=\"1\" selected>1</option>\n        <option value=\"2\">2</option>\n      </select>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"display:flex;align-items:flex-end;\">\n      <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"resetKA()\">Reset</button>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div style=\"margin-bottom:0.5rem;\">\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\"><span class=\"label\">bit #</span><div class=\"bits\" id=\"ka-bit-indices\"></div></div>\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\"><span class=\"label\">pattern</span><div class=\"bits\" id=\"ka-pattern-chars\"></div></div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"height:1px;background:var(--rule);margin:0.5rem 0;\"></div>\n  <div class=\"bitmask-row\" style=\"margin-bottom:0.4rem;\">\n    <span class=\"label\">text</span><div class=\"text-row\" id=\"ka-text-chars\"></div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"k-panel\" id=\"ka-layers\"></div>\n  <div id=\"ka-step-box\" style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.88rem;background:var(--accent-bg);border-radius:6px;padding:0.8rem 1rem;margin:0.75rem 0;min-height:3rem;\">\n    Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.6rem;flex-wrap:wrap;\">\n    <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" id=\"ka-next\" onclick=\"stepKA()\">Next Step</button>\n    <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"runAllKA()\">Run to end</button>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Bitap vs. the fzy scoring DP</h2>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"width:100%;margin:1rem 0;font-size:0.88rem;\">\n  <thead><tr><th>Property</th><th>Bitap (Shift-And/Or)</th><th>fzy scoring DP</th></tr></thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td>Matching model</td><td>Edit distance (k errors)</td><td>Subsequence</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Output</td><td>Match positions (yes/no + where)</td><td>Score (for ranking)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Time per candidate</td><td>O(m·n / w) — bit-parallel</td><td>O(m·n)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Pattern length limit</td><td>~64 chars (one CPU word)</td><td>No hard limit</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Ranking support</td><td>No — binary result</td><td>Yes — continuous score</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Used by</td><td><code>agrep</code>, <code>fzf</code> (inner loop)</td><td><code>fzy</code>, VS Code picker</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">They solve different halves of the problem</span>\n  Bitap excels at the <em>matching</em> question: is this candidate within\n  k edits of the pattern, and where? The fzy scoring DP excels at the\n  <em>ranking</em> question: among candidates that match, which one did\n  the user most likely mean? Production fuzzy finders often combine both.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. In the Shift-And algorithm, what does it mean when bit <code>i</code> is set in the state bitmask <code>R</code> after processing text character <code>t[j]</code>?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> The text character at position j equals pattern character at position i</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> The first i+1 characters of the pattern have been matched ending at text position j</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> There are i errors remaining before the pattern is rejected</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> The pattern appears exactly i times in the text so far</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. Bit i being set means a match of the first i+1 pattern characters has just concluded at the current text position. When bit m-1 (the last one) is set, the full pattern matched.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. The update rule is <code>R = ((R &lt;&lt; 1) | 1) &amp; D[t]</code>. What is the purpose of the <code>| 1</code> step?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> It sets the final bit to signal that a complete match was found</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> It always opens a fresh potential match starting at pattern position 0</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> It resets the bitmask to zero when no match is active</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> It inverts the mask to handle substitution errors</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. OR-ing with 1 always sets bit 0, meaning: at every text position, try starting a new match. Without this, the algorithm could only find one non-overlapping match.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. Why is Bitap limited to patterns shorter than ~64 characters in practice?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> Longer patterns have too many characters for the alphabet table to store</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> The bitmask must fit in a single machine word (64 bits) to exploit bit-parallel operations</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> The algorithm uses recursion that overflows the stack beyond 64 characters</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> Text scanning becomes O(n²) once the pattern exceeds one cache line</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. Each bit in the state bitmask represents one pattern position. A 64-bit integer gives you 64 bits — one per pattern character. Longer patterns require multi-word bitmasks, losing much of the speed advantage.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. In the k-error extension, the layer <code>R[j]</code> receives <code>R[j-1]</code> (without a shift) as one of its inputs. Which edit operation does this represent?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> Substitution — replace the text character with the pattern character</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> Deletion — remove a character from the text</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> Insertion — advance the pattern without consuming a text character</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> Transposition — swap two adjacent characters</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','c','Correct. R[j-1] without a shift means: the pattern pointer advances (we matched a pattern character) but the text pointer does not (we consumed nothing). That is exactly inserting a character into the pattern — or equivalently, deleting from the text.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<h2>You've completed the curriculum</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Across these six lessons you built the fuzzy search algorithm from first\n  principles — each design decision motivated by a specific failure of the\n  previous approach:\n</p>\n\n<ol>\n  <li>Exact match fails → need a distance metric</li>\n  <li>Distance needs formal definition → Levenshtein edit distance</li>\n  <li>Naive recursion is exponential → dynamic programming table</li>\n  <li>Distance doesn't model abbreviations → subsequence gate</li>\n  <li>Subsequence gives no ranking → scoring DP with bonuses</li>\n  <li>Scoring DP is O(mn) per candidate → bit-parallel Bitap</li>\n</ol>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitap_algorithm\" target=\"_blank\">\n    Bitap algorithm — Wikipedia\n  </a>\n  — Read the \"Exact searching\" and \"Fuzzy searching\" sections. The pseudocode\n  there matches the stepper above exactly.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat for any clarification on bitmask operations, error layers, or how this compares to the scoring DP.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0005b-multiple-matches.html\">← Lesson 5b: Competing Alignments</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 6 of 6</span>\n  <span></span>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── NFA diagram ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction renderNFA(pattern, containerId) {\n  const el = document.getElementById(containerId);\n  let html = `<div class=\"nfa-state active\">q₀</div>`;\n  for (let i = 0; i < pattern.length; i++) {\n    html += `<div class=\"nfa-arrow\">\n      <span class=\"ch\">${pattern[i]}</span>\n      <div class=\"line\"></div>\n    </div>\n    <div class=\"nfa-state ${i === pattern.length-1 ? 'final' : ''}\">q${i+1}</div>`;\n  }\n  el.innerHTML = html;\n}\nrenderNFA('cat', 'nfa-cat');\n\n// ── Shared utilities ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction buildD(pattern) {\n  const D = {};\n  for (let i = 0; i < pattern.length; i++) {\n    const c = pattern[i].toLowerCase();\n    if (!D[c]) D[c] = 0;\n    D[c] |= (1 << i);\n  }\n  return D;\n}\n\nfunction renderBits(bits, m, container, matchBit) {\n  let html = '';\n  for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n    const on = (bits >> i) & 1;\n    let cls = on ? 'on' : 'off';\n    if (on && i === m - 1) cls = 'match';\n    html += `<div class=\"bit ${cls}\">${on}</div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById(container).innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nfunction renderTextChars(text, current, found, container) {\n  let html = '';\n  text.split('').forEach((ch, i) => {\n    let cls = 'future';\n    if (found && found.has(i)) cls = 'found';\n    else if (i < current) cls = 'past';\n    else if (i === current) cls = 'current';\n    html += `<div class=\"text-char ${cls}\">${ch}</div>`;\n  });\n  document.getElementById(container).innerHTML = html;\n}\n\n// ── Shift-And exact stepper ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\nlet saPattern, saText, saD, saR, saStep, saDone, saFound;\n\nfunction resetSA() {\n  saPattern = document.getElementById('sa-pattern').value.toLowerCase() || 'cat';\n  saText    = document.getElementById('sa-text').value.toLowerCase()    || 'concatenate';\n  saD = buildD(saPattern);\n  saR = 0; saStep = 0; saDone = false; saFound = new Set();\n\n  // Render static pattern header\n  const m = saPattern.length;\n  let idxHtml = '', patHtml = '';\n  for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n    idxHtml += `<div class=\"bit idx\">${i}</div>`;\n    patHtml += `<div class=\"bit off\" style=\"background:#f4f4f5;border-color:var(--rule);color:var(--ink)\">${saPattern[i]}</div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('bit-indices').innerHTML  = idxHtml;\n  document.getElementById('pattern-chars').innerHTML = patHtml;\n\n  renderTextChars(saText, -1, saFound, 'text-chars');\n  renderBits(0, m, 'r-bits');\n  document.getElementById('step-box').innerHTML = 'Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.';\n  document.getElementById('sa-next').disabled = false;\n  document.getElementById('sa-next').textContent = 'Next Step';\n}\n\nfunction stepSA() {\n  if (saDone) return;\n  const m = saPattern.length;\n  const t = saText[saStep].toLowerCase();\n  const mask = saD[t] || 0;\n  saR = ((saR << 1) | 1) & mask;\n\n  const isMatch = (saR >> (m - 1)) & 1;\n  if (isMatch) {\n    for (let i = saStep - m + 1; i <= saStep; i++) saFound.add(i);\n  }\n\n  renderTextChars(saText, saStep, saFound, 'text-chars');\n  renderBits(saR, m, 'r-bits');\n\n  const dBin = (mask >>> 0).toString(2).padStart(m, '0').split('').reverse().join('');\n  const rBin = (saR  >>> 0).toString(2).padStart(m, '0').split('').reverse().join('');\n\n  let msg = `<strong>Step ${saStep + 1}:</strong> text[${saStep}] = '<code>${saText[saStep]}</code>'<br>\n    D['${t}'] = <code>${dBin}</code> &nbsp;→&nbsp; R = ((R&lt;&lt;1)|1) &amp; D = <code>${rBin}</code>`;\n  if (isMatch) msg += `<br><span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;\">✓ Match found ending at position ${saStep}!</span>`;\n\n  document.getElementById('step-box').innerHTML = msg;\n  saStep++;\n\n  if (saStep >= saText.length) {\n    saDone = true;\n    document.getElementById('sa-next').disabled = true;\n    document.getElementById('step-box').innerHTML += `<br><br><em>Scan complete. ${saFound.size > 0 ? `Pattern matched at positions: ${[...saFound].sort((a,b)=>a-b).join(', ')}.` : 'No match found.'}</em>`;\n  }\n}\n\nfunction runAllSA() { while (!saDone) stepSA(); }\n\ndocument.getElementById('sa-pattern').addEventListener('input', resetSA);\ndocument.getElementById('sa-text').addEventListener('input', resetSA);\nresetSA();\n\n// ── k-approximate stepper ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nlet kaPattern, kaText, kaD, kaR, kaStep, kaDone, kaK, kaFound;\n\nfunction resetKA() {\n  kaPattern = document.getElementById('ka-pattern').value.toLowerCase() || 'comit';\n  kaText    = document.getElementById('ka-text').value.toLowerCase()    || 'git commit';\n  kaK       = parseInt(document.getElementById('ka-k').value);\n  kaD = buildD(kaPattern);\n  kaR = new Array(kaK + 1).fill(0);\n  kaStep = 0; kaDone = false; kaFound = new Set();\n\n  const m = kaPattern.length;\n  let idxHtml = '', patHtml = '';\n  for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n    idxHtml += `<div class=\"bit idx\">${i}</div>`;\n    patHtml += `<div class=\"bit off\" style=\"background:#f4f4f5;border-color:var(--rule);color:var(--ink)\">${kaPattern[i]}</div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('ka-bit-indices').innerHTML   = idxHtml;\n  document.getElementById('ka-pattern-chars').innerHTML = patHtml;\n\n  renderTextChars(kaText, -1, kaFound, 'ka-text-chars');\n  renderKALayers();\n  document.getElementById('ka-step-box').innerHTML = 'Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.';\n  document.getElementById('ka-next').disabled = false;\n}\n\nfunction renderKALayers() {\n  const m = kaPattern.length;\n  let html = '';\n  for (let j = 0; j <= kaK; j++) {\n    let bits = '';\n    for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n      const on = (kaR[j] >> i) & 1;\n      let cls = on ? 'on' : 'off';\n      if (on && i === m - 1) cls = 'match';\n      bits += `<div class=\"bit ${cls}\">${on}</div>`;\n    }\n    html += `<div class=\"k-row\">\n      <span class=\"k-label\">R[${j}]</span>\n      <div class=\"k-bits\">${bits}</div>\n      ${(kaR[j] >> (m-1)) & 1 ? `<span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;margin-left:0.5rem;font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.82rem;\">≤${j} error${j===1?'':'s'} match</span>` : ''}\n    </div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('ka-layers').innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nfunction stepKA() {\n  if (kaDone) return;\n  const m = kaPattern.length;\n  const t = kaText[kaStep].toLowerCase();\n  const mask = kaD[t] || 0;\n\n  const prevR = [...kaR];\n  // Update from high to low to avoid using updated values\n  for (let j = kaK; j >= 1; j--) {\n    kaR[j] = (\n      (((prevR[j] << 1) | 1) & mask)   // match\n      | (prevR[j-1] << 1)              // deletion\n      | prevR[j-1]                     // insertion\n      | ((prevR[j-1] << 1) & ~mask)   // substitution\n    );\n  }\n  kaR[0] = ((prevR[0] << 1) | 1) & mask;\n\n  let matchAt = -1;\n  for (let j = 0; j <= kaK; j++) {\n    if ((kaR[j] >> (m-1)) & 1) { matchAt = j; break; }\n  }\n  if (matchAt >= 0) {\n    for (let i = Math.max(0, kaStep - m); i <= kaStep; i++) kaFound.add(i);\n  }\n\n  renderTextChars(kaText, kaStep, kaFound, 'ka-text-chars');\n  renderKALayers();\n\n  let msg = `<strong>Step ${kaStep + 1}:</strong> text[${kaStep}] = '<code>${kaText[kaStep]}</code>', D['${t}'] = <code>${(mask>>>0).toString(2).padStart(m,'0').split('').reverse().join('')}</code>`;\n  if (matchAt >= 0) msg += `<br><span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;\">✓ Match with ≤${matchAt} error${matchAt===1?'':'s'} ending at position ${kaStep}!</span>`;\n\n  document.getElementById('ka-step-box').innerHTML = msg;\n  kaStep++;\n\n  if (kaStep >= kaText.length) {\n    kaDone = true;\n    document.getElementById('ka-next').disabled = true;\n    document.getElementById('ka-step-box').innerHTML += `<br><br><em>Scan complete.</em>`;\n  }\n}\n\nfunction runAllKA() { while (!kaDone) stepKA(); }\n\ndocument.getElementById('ka-pattern').addEventListener('input', resetKA);\ndocument.getElementById('ka-text').addEventListener('input', resetKA);\ndocument.getElementById('ka-k').addEventListener('change', resetKA);\nresetKA();\n\n// ── Quiz ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}

Opening in existing browser session.

Lesson 6 is open — the final one in the curriculum.

**What it covers:**

**Exact matching first (Shift-And):** The stepper shows `cat` in `concatenate` character by character. Each step displays the bitmask `R`, what `D[t]` looked like for that character, and the result. The three operations — shift, OR 1, AND D[t] — are visible as they happen. Watch how bit 0 lights up at every position (the `| 1`), how bits advance rightward as a match builds, and how the final bit (bit 2 for a 3-char pattern) fires when `cat` is found.

**k-approximate matching:** The second stepper runs `comit` against `git commit` with k=1. You get one bitmask per error level — R[0] for exact, R[1] for ≤1 error. Watch how R[1] keeps a live state even when R[0] dies, until the match in "commit" activates it.

**The closing comparison table** draws the line between Bitap and the fzy scoring DP: Bitap answers *"is it here?"* fast; fzy answers *"which one did you mean?"* precisely. Production tools use both.

---

That completes the curriculum. Every lesson answered one question: *what specific problem did this design decision solve?*

| Lesson | Problem | Decision |
|--------|---------|----------|
| 1 | Exact match misses typos and abbreviations | Frame the requirements |
| 2 | "Closeness" is intuitive, not computable | Levenshtein edit distance |
| 3 | Computing distance naively is exponential | DP table (Wagner-Fischer) |
| 4 | Distance is the wrong model for abbreviations | Subsequence gate |
| 5+5b | Subsequence gives no ranking | Scoring DP with bonuses |
| 6 | Scoring DP is O(mn) per candidate | Bitap bit-parallelism |

padding: 0 2px; }\n  </style>\n</head>\n<body>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-header\">\n  <div class=\"lesson-meta\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 6 of 6</div>\n  <h1>The Bitap Algorithm</h1>\n  <p class=\"lesson-subtitle\">The design decision: use bit-parallelism to make approximate matching fast</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2>The problem this lesson solves</h2>\n\n<p>\n  The scoring DP from Lessons 5 and 5b runs in O(|query| × |candidate|) time\n  — polynomial, but still non-trivial when you have thousands of candidates.\n  The subsequence gate filters most of them, but a different class of\n  problems needs something faster still: <em>scanning large bodies of text</em>\n  for approximate matches, without any pre-filtering.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Design decision</span>\n  Represent the matching state as a <strong>bitmask</strong>, where each bit\n  tracks whether a particular prefix of the pattern has been matched ending\n  at the current text position. A single bitwise operation advances\n  <em>all states at once</em>, exploiting the CPU's 64-bit word to do 64\n  comparisons in one instruction. This is the <strong>Bitap algorithm</strong>\n  (also called Shift-Or or Shift-And), introduced by Baeza-Yates and\n  Gonnet (1992).\n</div>\n\n<h2>The NFA intuition</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Before bitmasks, think of matching as a\n  <strong>non-deterministic finite automaton (NFA)</strong>.\n  For pattern <code>cat</code>, the NFA has one state per pattern character\n  plus a start state:\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"nfa-diagram\" id=\"nfa-cat\">\n  <!-- rendered by JS -->\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  The NFA starts in state 0. Each time a text character matches the expected\n  pattern character, the NFA moves to the next state. <em>Multiple states\n  can be active simultaneously</em> — this is the non-determinism.\n  If we ever reach the final state, we found a match.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">The bitmask insight</span>\n  Instead of tracking which states are active in a set, encode them as\n  a single integer: bit <code>i</code> is 1 if state <code>i</code> is active.\n  One bitwise operation advances all active states at once.\n</div>\n\n<h2>The Shift-And algorithm (exact matching)</h2>\n\n<p>\n  <strong>Precomputation</strong>: for each character <code>c</code> in the alphabet,\n  build a mask <code>D[c]</code> where bit <code>i</code> is 1 if\n  <code>pattern[i] == c</code>.\n</p>\n\n<p>\n  <strong>Scanning</strong>: maintain a state bitmask <code>R</code>\n  (initially 0). For each text character <code>t</code>:\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"algo-box\">\n<span class=\"comment\">// Shift all active states forward by one, open a new state 0, keep only</span><br>\n<span class=\"comment\">// states where the pattern character matches the current text character.</span><br>\n<br>\nR = ((R <span class=\"hl\">&lt;&lt; 1</span>) | 1) <span class=\"hl\">&amp;</span> D[t]<br>\n<br>\n<span class=\"comment\">// If bit (m-1) is set in R, the full pattern was just matched.</span><br>\n<span class=\"kw\">if</span> (R &amp; (1 &lt;&lt; (m-1))) → match found\n</div>\n\n<p>Each line decodes as:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li><code>R &lt;&lt; 1</code> — advance every active state by one position in the pattern</li>\n  <li><code>| 1</code> — always try starting a fresh match at position 0</li>\n  <li><code>&amp; D[t]</code> — discard any state where the pattern character does not match the text character</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2>Step through it</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Watch the bitmask evolve as we scan the text.\n  Bits are shown from position 0 (left) to m−1 (right).\n  A lit bit means \"a match of this many pattern chars has just been completed.\"\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"demo\" style=\"padding:1.1rem 1.2rem;\">\n  <h3>Shift-And stepper</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.85rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:100px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Pattern</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sa-pattern\" value=\"cat\" maxlength=\"8\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:3;min-width:180px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Text</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"sa-text\" value=\"concatenate\" maxlength=\"20\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"display:flex;align-items:flex-end;\">\n      <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"resetSA()\">Reset</button>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <!-- Pattern character labels -->\n  <div style=\"margin-bottom:0.3rem;\">\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\">\n      <span class=\"label\">bit #</span>\n      <div class=\"bits\" id=\"bit-indices\"></div>\n    </div>\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\">\n      <span class=\"label\">pattern</span>\n      <div class=\"bits\" id=\"pattern-chars\"></div>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div style=\"height:1px;background:var(--rule);margin:0.6rem 0;\"></div>\n\n  <!-- Text display -->\n  <div class=\"bitmask-row\" style=\"margin-bottom:0.4rem;\">\n    <span class=\"label\">text</span>\n    <div class=\"text-row\" id=\"text-chars\"></div>\n  </div>\n\n  <!-- State R -->\n  <div class=\"bitmask-row\">\n    <span class=\"label\">R</span>\n    <div class=\"bits\" id=\"r-bits\"></div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div id=\"step-box\">Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.</div>\n\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.6rem;flex-wrap:wrap;\">\n    <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" id=\"sa-next\" onclick=\"stepSA()\">Next Step</button>\n    <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"runAllSA()\">Run to end</button>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Extending to k errors (approximate matching)</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Exact matching is useful, but fuzzy search needs tolerance for errors.\n  The Bitap algorithm extends cleanly: instead of one bitmask, maintain\n  <strong>k + 1 bitmasks</strong>, one per error level.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"algo-box\">\n<span class=\"comment\">// R[j] = states reachable with exactly j errors</span><br>\n<span class=\"kw\">for</span> j = k <span class=\"kw\">downto</span> 1:<br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;R[j] = (<br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;((R[j] &lt;&lt; 1) | 1) &amp; D[t]   <span class=\"comment\">// match (same as exact)</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;| (R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1)             <span class=\"comment\">// deletion from text</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;| R[j-1]                      <span class=\"comment\">// insertion into text</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;| (R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1) &amp; ~D[t]      <span class=\"comment\">// substitution</span><br>\n&nbsp;&nbsp;)<br>\nR[0] = ((R[0] &lt;&lt; 1) | 1) &amp; D[t]   <span class=\"comment\">// exact match layer</span>\n</div>\n\n<p>\n  Each layer adds a one-step \"rescue\" from the layer below it. A state that\n  would have died (wrong character) in layer j−1 gets propagated to layer j\n  with one more error counted.\n</p>\n\n<div class=\"callout note\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">Mapping to edit operations</span>\n  <ul style=\"margin-top:0.4rem;\">\n    <li><code>R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1</code> (no AND with D[t]) — <strong>deletion</strong>: skip a text character</li>\n    <li><code>R[j-1]</code> — <strong>insertion</strong>: advance in pattern without consuming text</li>\n    <li><code>(R[j-1] &lt;&lt; 1) &amp; ~D[t]</code> — <strong>substitution</strong>: consume text but allow mismatch</li>\n  </ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Try it: k-approximate matching</h2>\n\n<div class=\"demo\" style=\"padding:1.1rem 1.2rem;\">\n  <h3>Approximate match stepper (k errors)</h3>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.75rem;flex-wrap:wrap;margin-bottom:0.75rem;\">\n    <div style=\"flex:1;min-width:80px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Pattern</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"ka-pattern\" value=\"comit\" maxlength=\"8\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:3;min-width:160px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">Text</label>\n      <input type=\"text\" id=\"ka-text\" value=\"git commit\" maxlength=\"20\" autocomplete=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"width:100%;\">\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"flex:0.5;min-width:60px;\">\n      <label style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.78rem;color:var(--muted);display:block;margin-bottom:0.25rem;\">k</label>\n      <select id=\"ka-k\" style=\"width:100%;padding:0.45rem 0.3rem;border:1px solid var(--rule);border-radius:4px;\">\n        <option value=\"0\">0</option>\n        <option value=\"1\" selected>1</option>\n        <option value=\"2\">2</option>\n      </select>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"display:flex;align-items:flex-end;\">\n      <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"resetKA()\">Reset</button>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div style=\"margin-bottom:0.5rem;\">\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\"><span class=\"label\">bit #</span><div class=\"bits\" id=\"ka-bit-indices\"></div></div>\n    <div class=\"bitmask-row\"><span class=\"label\">pattern</span><div class=\"bits\" id=\"ka-pattern-chars\"></div></div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"height:1px;background:var(--rule);margin:0.5rem 0;\"></div>\n  <div class=\"bitmask-row\" style=\"margin-bottom:0.4rem;\">\n    <span class=\"label\">text</span><div class=\"text-row\" id=\"ka-text-chars\"></div>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"k-panel\" id=\"ka-layers\"></div>\n  <div id=\"ka-step-box\" style=\"font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.88rem;background:var(--accent-bg);border-radius:6px;padding:0.8rem 1rem;margin:0.75rem 0;min-height:3rem;\">\n    Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"display:flex;gap:0.6rem;flex-wrap:wrap;\">\n    <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" id=\"ka-next\" onclick=\"stepKA()\">Next Step</button>\n    <button class=\"btn btn-ghost\" onclick=\"runAllKA()\">Run to end</button>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Bitap vs. the fzy scoring DP</h2>\n\n<table class=\"dp-table\" style=\"width:100%;margin:1rem 0;font-size:0.88rem;\">\n  <thead><tr><th>Property</th><th>Bitap (Shift-And/Or)</th><th>fzy scoring DP</th></tr></thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr><td>Matching model</td><td>Edit distance (k errors)</td><td>Subsequence</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Output</td><td>Match positions (yes/no + where)</td><td>Score (for ranking)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Time per candidate</td><td>O(m·n / w) — bit-parallel</td><td>O(m·n)</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Pattern length limit</td><td>~64 chars (one CPU word)</td><td>No hard limit</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Ranking support</td><td>No — binary result</td><td>Yes — continuous score</td></tr>\n    <tr><td>Used by</td><td><code>agrep</code>, <code>fzf</code> (inner loop)</td><td><code>fzy</code>, VS Code picker</td></tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<div class=\"callout insight\">\n  <span class=\"callout-label\">They solve different halves of the problem</span>\n  Bitap excels at the <em>matching</em> question: is this candidate within\n  k edits of the pattern, and where? The fzy scoring DP excels at the\n  <em>ranking</em> question: among candidates that match, which one did\n  the user most likely mean? Production fuzzy finders often combine both.\n</div>\n\n<h2>Quiz: Check your understanding</h2>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q1\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q1. In the Shift-And algorithm, what does it mean when bit <code>i</code> is set in the state bitmask <code>R</code> after processing text character <code>t[j]</code>?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"a\"> The text character at position j equals pattern character at position i</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"b\"> The first i+1 characters of the pattern have been matched ending at text position j</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"c\"> There are i errors remaining before the pattern is rejected</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q1\" value=\"d\"> The pattern appears exactly i times in the text so far</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q1','b','Correct. Bit i being set means a match of the first i+1 pattern characters has just concluded at the current text position. When bit m-1 (the last one) is set, the full pattern matched.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q1-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q2\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q2. The update rule is <code>R = ((R &lt;&lt; 1) | 1) &amp; D[t]</code>. What is the purpose of the <code>| 1</code> step?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"a\"> It sets the final bit to signal that a complete match was found</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"b\"> It always opens a fresh potential match starting at pattern position 0</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"c\"> It resets the bitmask to zero when no match is active</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q2\" value=\"d\"> It inverts the mask to handle substitution errors</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q2','b','Correct. OR-ing with 1 always sets bit 0, meaning: at every text position, try starting a new match. Without this, the algorithm could only find one non-overlapping match.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q2-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q3\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q3. Why is Bitap limited to patterns shorter than ~64 characters in practice?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"a\"> Longer patterns have too many characters for the alphabet table to store</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"b\"> The bitmask must fit in a single machine word (64 bits) to exploit bit-parallel operations</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"c\"> The algorithm uses recursion that overflows the stack beyond 64 characters</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q3\" value=\"d\"> Text scanning becomes O(n²) once the pattern exceeds one cache line</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q3','b','Correct. Each bit in the state bitmask represents one pattern position. A 64-bit integer gives you 64 bits — one per pattern character. Longer patterns require multi-word bitmasks, losing much of the speed advantage.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q3-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"quiz\" id=\"q4\">\n  <p class=\"quiz-question\">Q4. In the k-error extension, the layer <code>R[j]</code> receives <code>R[j-1]</code> (without a shift) as one of its inputs. Which edit operation does this represent?</p>\n  <ul class=\"quiz-options\">\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"a\"> Substitution — replace the text character with the pattern character</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"b\"> Deletion — remove a character from the text</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"c\"> Insertion — advance the pattern without consuming a text character</label></li>\n    <li><label><input type=\"radio\" name=\"q4\" value=\"d\"> Transposition — swap two adjacent characters</label></li>\n  </ul>\n  <button class=\"btn btn-primary\" onclick=\"checkQ('q4','c','Correct. R[j-1] without a shift means: the pattern pointer advances (we matched a pattern character) but the text pointer does not (we consumed nothing). That is exactly inserting a character into the pattern — or equivalently, deleting from the text.')\">Check</button>\n  <p class=\"quiz-feedback\" id=\"q4-feedback\"></p>\n</div>\n\n<hr>\n\n<h2>You've completed the curriculum</h2>\n\n<p>\n  Across these six lessons you built the fuzzy search algorithm from first\n  principles — each design decision motivated by a specific failure of the\n  previous approach:\n</p>\n\n<ol>\n  <li>Exact match fails → need a distance metric</li>\n  <li>Distance needs formal definition → Levenshtein edit distance</li>\n  <li>Naive recursion is exponential → dynamic programming table</li>\n  <li>Distance doesn't model abbreviations → subsequence gate</li>\n  <li>Subsequence gives no ranking → scoring DP with bonuses</li>\n  <li>Scoring DP is O(mn) per candidate → bit-parallel Bitap</li>\n</ol>\n\n<div class=\"primary-source\">\n  <span class=\"label\">Primary source for this lesson</span>\n  <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitap_algorithm\" target=\"_blank\">\n    Bitap algorithm — Wikipedia\n  </a>\n  — Read the \"Exact searching\" and \"Fuzzy searching\" sections. The pseudocode\n  there matches the stepper above exactly.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"ask-teacher\">\n  💬 <strong>Have a question?</strong> Ask your teacher — type in the chat for any clarification on bitmask operations, error layers, or how this compares to the scoring DP.\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"lesson-nav\">\n  <a href=\"0005b-multiple-matches.html\">← Lesson 5b: Competing Alignments</a>\n  <span class=\"center\">Fuzzy Search · Lesson 6 of 6</span>\n  <span></span>\n</div>\n\n<script>\n// ── NFA diagram ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction renderNFA(pattern, containerId) {\n  const el = document.getElementById(containerId);\n  let html = `<div class=\"nfa-state active\">q₀</div>`;\n  for (let i = 0; i < pattern.length; i++) {\n    html += `<div class=\"nfa-arrow\">\n      <span class=\"ch\">${pattern[i]}</span>\n      <div class=\"line\"></div>\n    </div>\n    <div class=\"nfa-state ${i === pattern.length-1 ? 'final' : ''}\">q${i+1}</div>`;\n  }\n  el.innerHTML = html;\n}\nrenderNFA('cat', 'nfa-cat');\n\n// ── Shared utilities ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction buildD(pattern) {\n  const D = {};\n  for (let i = 0; i < pattern.length; i++) {\n    const c = pattern[i].toLowerCase();\n    if (!D[c]) D[c] = 0;\n    D[c] |= (1 << i);\n  }\n  return D;\n}\n\nfunction renderBits(bits, m, container, matchBit) {\n  let html = '';\n  for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n    const on = (bits >> i) & 1;\n    let cls = on ? 'on' : 'off';\n    if (on && i === m - 1) cls = 'match';\n    html += `<div class=\"bit ${cls}\">${on}</div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById(container).innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nfunction renderTextChars(text, current, found, container) {\n  let html = '';\n  text.split('').forEach((ch, i) => {\n    let cls = 'future';\n    if (found && found.has(i)) cls = 'found';\n    else if (i < current) cls = 'past';\n    else if (i === current) cls = 'current';\n    html += `<div class=\"text-char ${cls}\">${ch}</div>`;\n  });\n  document.getElementById(container).innerHTML = html;\n}\n\n// ── Shift-And exact stepper ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\nlet saPattern, saText, saD, saR, saStep, saDone, saFound;\n\nfunction resetSA() {\n  saPattern = document.getElementById('sa-pattern').value.toLowerCase() || 'cat';\n  saText    = document.getElementById('sa-text').value.toLowerCase()    || 'concatenate';\n  saD = buildD(saPattern);\n  saR = 0; saStep = 0; saDone = false; saFound = new Set();\n\n  // Render static pattern header\n  const m = saPattern.length;\n  let idxHtml = '', patHtml = '';\n  for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n    idxHtml += `<div class=\"bit idx\">${i}</div>`;\n    patHtml += `<div class=\"bit off\" style=\"background:#f4f4f5;border-color:var(--rule);color:var(--ink)\">${saPattern[i]}</div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('bit-indices').innerHTML  = idxHtml;\n  document.getElementById('pattern-chars').innerHTML = patHtml;\n\n  renderTextChars(saText, -1, saFound, 'text-chars');\n  renderBits(0, m, 'r-bits');\n  document.getElementById('step-box').innerHTML = 'Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.';\n  document.getElementById('sa-next').disabled = false;\n  document.getElementById('sa-next').textContent = 'Next Step';\n}\n\nfunction stepSA() {\n  if (saDone) return;\n  const m = saPattern.length;\n  const t = saText[saStep].toLowerCase();\n  const mask = saD[t] || 0;\n  saR = ((saR << 1) | 1) & mask;\n\n  const isMatch = (saR >> (m - 1)) & 1;\n  if (isMatch) {\n    for (let i = saStep - m + 1; i <= saStep; i++) saFound.add(i);\n  }\n\n  renderTextChars(saText, saStep, saFound, 'text-chars');\n  renderBits(saR, m, 'r-bits');\n\n  const dBin = (mask >>> 0).toString(2).padStart(m, '0').split('').reverse().join('');\n  const rBin = (saR  >>> 0).toString(2).padStart(m, '0').split('').reverse().join('');\n\n  let msg = `<strong>Step ${saStep + 1}:</strong> text[${saStep}] = '<code>${saText[saStep]}</code>'<br>\n    D['${t}'] = <code>${dBin}</code> &nbsp;→&nbsp; R = ((R&lt;&lt;1)|1) &amp; D = <code>${rBin}</code>`;\n  if (isMatch) msg += `<br><span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;\">✓ Match found ending at position ${saStep}!</span>`;\n\n  document.getElementById('step-box').innerHTML = msg;\n  saStep++;\n\n  if (saStep >= saText.length) {\n    saDone = true;\n    document.getElementById('sa-next').disabled = true;\n    document.getElementById('step-box').innerHTML += `<br><br><em>Scan complete. ${saFound.size > 0 ? `Pattern matched at positions: ${[...saFound].sort((a,b)=>a-b).join(', ')}.` : 'No match found.'}</em>`;\n  }\n}\n\nfunction runAllSA() { while (!saDone) stepSA(); }\n\ndocument.getElementById('sa-pattern').addEventListener('input', resetSA);\ndocument.getElementById('sa-text').addEventListener('input', resetSA);\nresetSA();\n\n// ── k-approximate stepper ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nlet kaPattern, kaText, kaD, kaR, kaStep, kaDone, kaK, kaFound;\n\nfunction resetKA() {\n  kaPattern = document.getElementById('ka-pattern').value.toLowerCase() || 'comit';\n  kaText    = document.getElementById('ka-text').value.toLowerCase()    || 'git commit';\n  kaK       = parseInt(document.getElementById('ka-k').value);\n  kaD = buildD(kaPattern);\n  kaR = new Array(kaK + 1).fill(0);\n  kaStep = 0; kaDone = false; kaFound = new Set();\n\n  const m = kaPattern.length;\n  let idxHtml = '', patHtml = '';\n  for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n    idxHtml += `<div class=\"bit idx\">${i}</div>`;\n    patHtml += `<div class=\"bit off\" style=\"background:#f4f4f5;border-color:var(--rule);color:var(--ink)\">${kaPattern[i]}</div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('ka-bit-indices').innerHTML   = idxHtml;\n  document.getElementById('ka-pattern-chars').innerHTML = patHtml;\n\n  renderTextChars(kaText, -1, kaFound, 'ka-text-chars');\n  renderKALayers();\n  document.getElementById('ka-step-box').innerHTML = 'Press <strong>Next Step</strong> to begin.';\n  document.getElementById('ka-next').disabled = false;\n}\n\nfunction renderKALayers() {\n  const m = kaPattern.length;\n  let html = '';\n  for (let j = 0; j <= kaK; j++) {\n    let bits = '';\n    for (let i = 0; i < m; i++) {\n      const on = (kaR[j] >> i) & 1;\n      let cls = on ? 'on' : 'off';\n      if (on && i === m - 1) cls = 'match';\n      bits += `<div class=\"bit ${cls}\">${on}</div>`;\n    }\n    html += `<div class=\"k-row\">\n      <span class=\"k-label\">R[${j}]</span>\n      <div class=\"k-bits\">${bits}</div>\n      ${(kaR[j] >> (m-1)) & 1 ? `<span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;margin-left:0.5rem;font-family:var(--sans);font-size:0.82rem;\">≤${j} error${j===1?'':'s'} match</span>` : ''}\n    </div>`;\n  }\n  document.getElementById('ka-layers').innerHTML = html;\n}\n\nfunction stepKA() {\n  if (kaDone) return;\n  const m = kaPattern.length;\n  const t = kaText[kaStep].toLowerCase();\n  const mask = kaD[t] || 0;\n\n  const prevR = [...kaR];\n  // Update from high to low to avoid using updated values\n  for (let j = kaK; j >= 1; j--) {\n    kaR[j] = (\n      (((prevR[j] << 1) | 1) & mask)   // match\n      | (prevR[j-1] << 1)              // deletion\n      | prevR[j-1]                     // insertion\n      | ((prevR[j-1] << 1) & ~mask)   // substitution\n    );\n  }\n  kaR[0] = ((prevR[0] << 1) | 1) & mask;\n\n  let matchAt = -1;\n  for (let j = 0; j <= kaK; j++) {\n    if ((kaR[j] >> (m-1)) & 1) { matchAt = j; break; }\n  }\n  if (matchAt >= 0) {\n    for (let i = Math.max(0, kaStep - m); i <= kaStep; i++) kaFound.add(i);\n  }\n\n  renderTextChars(kaText, kaStep, kaFound, 'ka-text-chars');\n  renderKALayers();\n\n  let msg = `<strong>Step ${kaStep + 1}:</strong> text[${kaStep}] = '<code>${kaText[kaStep]}</code>', D['${t}'] = <code>${(mask>>>0).toString(2).padStart(m,'0').split('').reverse().join('')}</code>`;\n  if (matchAt >= 0) msg += `<br><span style=\"color:var(--success);font-weight:700;\">✓ Match with ≤${matchAt} error${matchAt===1?'':'s'} ending at position ${kaStep}!</span>`;\n\n  document.getElementById('ka-step-box').innerHTML = msg;\n  kaStep++;\n\n  if (kaStep >= kaText.length) {\n    kaDone = true;\n    document.getElementById('ka-next').disabled = true;\n    document.getElementById('ka-step-box').innerHTML += `<br><br><em>Scan complete.</em>`;\n  }\n}\n\nfunction runAllKA() { while (!kaDone) stepKA(); }\n\ndocument.getElementById('ka-pattern').addEventListener('input', resetKA);\ndocument.getElementById('ka-text').addEventListener('input', resetKA);\ndocument.getElementById('ka-k').addEventListener('change', resetKA);\nresetKA();\n\n// ── Quiz ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\nfunction checkQ(id, correct, explanation) {\n  const selected = document.querySelector(`input[name=\"${id}\"]:checked`);\n  const feedback = document.getElementById(`${id}-feedback`);\n  if (!selected) { feedback.textContent = 'Please select an answer.'; feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback'; return; }\n  document.querySelectorAll(`input[name=\"${id}\"]`).forEach(r => {\n    const lbl = r.closest('label');\n    if (r.value === correct) lbl.classList.add('correct');\n    else if (r.checked)      lbl.classList.add('wrong');\n    r.disabled = true;\n  });\n  if (selected.value === correct) {\n    feedback.textContent = '✓ ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback correct';\n  } else {\n    feedback.textContent = '✗ Not quite. ' + explanation;\n    feedback.className = 'quiz-feedback wrong';\n  }\n}\n</script>\n\n</body>\n</html>\n"
}
```
